# Slice history — shipped work (read on demand)

> The running per-slice changelog + the deep per-slice rationale (this file IS the canonical narrative; it
> also lives in the squash-merge commits). CLAUDE.md holds only the current head pointer.
> **Migration head: `0070` (next `0071`).** Code: https://github.com/CoJoA13/EasySynQ (`main` protected, PR + green CI).

## DISTRIBUTION — the on-prem install path (doc 03 §12; the roadmap's air-gap/appliance seed)

> The product was feature-complete but only installable by a developer (compose + a hand-tended `.env`).
> The owner's production target is Windows Server + Hyper-V with the QMS tree on an SMB share — the
> appliance is the near-1-click path onto that box, and the vehicle for the AHT dogfood import (UJ-2).

### S-appliance — the 1-click Hyper-V appliance: VHDX + seed ISO + PS installer (infra+scripts+docs only; NO migration [head stays `0070`]; NO new key [catalog 102]; NO api/web source change except `scripts/install.sh`; PR #313 squash `2f4be28`)

**What shipped — a three-file hand-off (`EasySynQ-appliance.vhdx` + `EasySynQ-seed.iso` + `Install-EasySynQ.ps1`) that stands up the full stack on Windows Server Hyper-V: copy, run one elevated PS script, browse to `https://easysynq.local`, complete the wizard.** `infra/appliance/build-appliance.sh` builds both artifacts on any Linux box with NO root: download + SHA256SUMS-verify the Ubuntu 24.04 cloud image → `qemu-img convert` to dynamic VHDX (the OS disk ships as the UNMODIFIED upstream image — all provisioning is plain text on the seed, auditable pre-run) + a `cidata` NoCloud seed ISO via **pycdlib** (pure-python — no mtools/genisoimage/root; `uv run --with pycdlib`) carrying user-data/meta-data + the **pinned repo bundle** (`git archive HEAD`, 4.3MB) + the provision payload. A THIN cloud-init (console user `easysynq`, forced password change, base packages incl. `linux-cloud-tools-virtual`) hands off to **`easysynq-provision`** — a systemd **oneshot** (`TimeoutStartSec=infinity`, `RemainAfterExit`) whose every step is skip-if-done so `systemctl restart` resumes any failure: seed re-mount by label → atomic repo extract (tmp+`mv`+stamp) → `.env` via the new **`EASYSYNQ_ENV_ONLY=1` install.sh mode** + a fail-closed scoped `CHANGE_ME` check → appliance env overrides (`SITE_ADDRESS=https://easysynq.local`, internal OIDC JWKS/discovery, `S3_PUBLIC_ENDPOINT=https://easysynq.local:9443`, `IMPORT_SOURCE_PATH=/srv/easysynq/import` FIXED so the QMS-share mount never edits .env) → `compose up -d --build` over FOUR files (base + s + **airgap** [tls internal] + **appliance**) → readyz gate (`curl --resolve` for SNI) → the initial Keycloak account (`qmsadmin`, `--temporary` password) → mint the one-time bootstrap secret → a 0600 hand-off sheet + a dual-console banner (tty1 for Hyper-V, ttyS0 for serial watchers). Day-2 helpers in `/usr/local/bin`: `easysynq-status` (+`--remint`, +`--ca` printing Caddy's root CA for the GPO rollout), `easysynq-create-user`, `easysynq-mount-qms` (READ-ONLY CIFS at the fixed import root; restarts api+worker because **a bind mount never sees a filesystem mounted over it post-start**), `easysynq-reconfigure --host <fqdn>` (mDNS→AD DNS: rewrites site/presign/issuer + kcadm-appends the redirect URI), `easysynq-compose` (the ONE overlay-set invocation). `compose.appliance.yml` + `Caddyfile.appliance`: the browser-facing **MinIO TLS site on :9443** (presigned URLs fetched from an https page are MIXED-CONTENT-blocked on plain :9000; Caddy `reverse_proxy` preserves Host so **SigV4 still validates**) and `ports: !reset []` on minio (compose merges ports ADDITIVELY — the dev-only plaintext :9000 publish from compose.s.yml would otherwise ship on the LAN); the appliance Caddyfile `import`s the base mounted at `Caddyfile.base` (compose volumes MERGE BY TARGET → the entry Caddyfile is swapped, one source of truth, the base's global options block stays first because import splices tokens). `Install-EasySynQ.ps1`: Gen2 VM, `-SecureBootTemplate MicrosoftUEFICertificateAuthority`, EXTERNAL-vswitch detection with create-guidance, golden-image copy + `Resize-VHD` (cloud-init growpart expands), DVD seed, first-boot-device pin, IP wait — with **hostname-only URL messaging** (TLS + the OIDC issuer are bound to `easysynq.local`; a bare-IP URL cannot work). Plus `docs/runbooks/appliance-install.md` (GPO CA distribution, QMS-share mount, custom hostname, troubleshooting, sizing) and the committed **`boot-test.sh` QEMU/KVM harness** (two-phase: fresh provision to a verdict, then a SAME-DISK reboot proving the stack self-recovers with the provision unit no-op'ing on its stamp).

⚠ **The headline product fix is OUTSIDE the appliance: `scripts/install.sh` shipped every fresh install's app on the DB OWNER role** — `set_kv DATABASE_URL …easysynq:${PG_PW}…` overwrote `.env.example`'s `easysynq_app` DSN, silently defeating the S6 append-only REVOKEs (the review's "dev-grade .env" MAJOR). Fixed at the source for ALL installs: generate `APP_PW`/`LINKER_PW`, point `DATABASE_URL` at `easysynq_app`, seed `AUDIT_LINKER_DATABASE_URL` + `APP_DB_PASSWORD`/`LINKER_DB_PASSWORD` (the 0010 migration creates the roles from these), keep `DATABASE_URL_SYNC` on the owner (alembic/backup). The boot test then EXERCISES this end-to-end (fresh DB → 70 migrations → the app serving readyz as the non-owner role).

⚠ **Traps this slice burned into the record.** (1) **`git archive` ships HEAD, not the working tree** — the first boot test ran a seed missing the uncommitted compose overlay (caught pre-boot by the in-VM path check would've been a compose-file-not-found; caught here by inspection) → the builder now REFUSES a dirty tree (`ALLOW_DIRTY=1` override). (2) **`git add -A` before the `.gitignore` existed committed the 593MB qcow2 + the 620MB image cache into branch history, and a later gitignore NEVER unstages** — caught by `git archive | wc -c` ballooning to 616MB (the seed ISO hit 589MB); fixed by a `reset --soft origin/main` history rewrite (nothing had been pushed) + `git rm -r --cached -f`. (3) **A VM disk in the harness scratchpad is a host-killer on this box: `/tmp` is a 7.2G tmpfs** — the guest's docker builds grew the qcow2 to 5.7G, filled the tmpfs, and the harness's OWN shell died silently (every command exit 1, zero output, sandboxed or not; subagent shells too) — `df -h /tmp` is the FIRST diagnostic for that symptom, the Monitor tool's spawn path is the escape hatch, and `boot-test.sh` hard-defaults its work dir to `~/.cache`. (4) **The `[EasySynQ] READY` banner went to /dev/tty1 only — invisible to the serial console a QEMU watcher tails** → run #3 PASSED (systemd `Finished easysynq-provision` proves every gate: readyz, account, secret) while the watcher timed out → `console()` now dual-writes tty1+ttyS0 and the watcher accepts the systemd line as the fallback verdict. (5) **`tr </dev/urandom | head` under `set -euo pipefail` dies of SIGPIPE deterministically** (tr's write to the closed pipe → exit 141 → errexit) — the documented no-args `easysynq-create-user` path was dead on arrival; use the finite-input `openssl rand | tr | head` gen_secret shape. (6) **A fail-closed `CHANGE_ME` guard must scope to the keys install.sh GENERATES** — `AUDIT_SINK_SECRET_KEY` keeps its placeholder BY DESIGN (the R13 off-host sink is operator-configured at the wizard's soft gate); the broad grep crash-looped run #2 (which at least proved the FAILED banner + resume path live). (7) **Root-generated 0600 `.env` breaks every sudo-less helper** (status/--remint/compose read it as the console user) → `root:easysynq` 0640 (no exposure — the user is docker-group root-equivalent).

**Review + verification.** A 3-lens adversarial workflow (diff-critic · a Hyper-V/PowerShell expert lens [the one thing unexecutable off-Windows] · a first-boot ops-failure-modes lens) with per-finding refutation: **24 raw → 22 confirmed → 13 distinct, ALL folded** (the two refuted: an SSH-password-auth takeover claim — cloud images ship password auth OFF — and a no-defect placeholder). The mid-review harness outage (trap 3) forced a transcript-level reconstruction of the verdicts (the workflow's output file was empty — the result had lived only in the truncated notification; `agent-*.jsonl` + the StructuredOutput calls are the durable record). **Boot-proven on the SHIPPED artifact:** the VHDX round-tripped to qcow2 under QEMU/KVM — fresh provision verdict ~220s, host-side `/readyz` green through the TLS port-forward, same-disk reboot green. **Named-not-faked deferrals:** the PS script's first REAL Hyper-V execution is on the owner's server (expert-reviewed, verbose, idempotent-ish; the external-vswitch step is the likeliest first speed bump) · no prebuilt-images air-gap bundle yet (first boot pulls/builds; `images.lock` digest-pinning + `compose.airgap.yml` are the reserved rails) · kcadm admin password on the container-exec argv (single-admin VM, accepted) · no appliance auto-update story (rebuild + reprovision is the v1 path) · the `easysynq-status --ca` copy path is console copy/paste (no SSH keys provisioned by default). **Tests:** api unit **1078 unchanged** · web **1306 unchanged** (nothing in the suites reaches this surface — the QEMU boot test IS the proof; both gates re-run green pre-PR). (S-appliance, infra+scripts+docs, NO migration [head `0070`], NO new key [catalog 102], PR #313 squash `2f4be28`.)

## NOTIFICATIONS — the in-app + email notification system (clause-agnostic; doc 10 §9, R53)

> The biggest remaining functional gap after the register arc: the workflow engine + My Tasks created `Task`
> rows, but **nothing reached users by email**. doc 10 §9 specs the full target (dual in-app + email, a
> 16-event catalog, versioned templates, a per-user digest matrix, quiet hours, escalation timers, owned
> bounces) — ~5 slices. **Roadmap:** slice 1 the BE spine + email (this) · **slice 2** the SPA bell/center ·
> **slice 3** preferences + digests + quiet hours (+ DOC_ACK email + the `/settings/notifications` route) ·
> **slice 4** escalation timers (`SlaPolicy`/`working_calendar`, R29) · **slice 5** awareness events
> (`doc.released`/…) + the Health-dashboard delivery-failure panel. **slice 5 split into 5a (awareness
> events) · 5b (Health panel + admin Config tab) · 5c (SSE).**

### S-capa-overdue — CAPA target-completion date + overdue notification (closes the last class-mapped-but-unwired event `capa.overdue`; BE+FE+CLI; migration **0070** [head `0069→0070`]; PR #302 squash `bdd4fd5`)

**What shipped — `capa.overdue` end-to-end.** A CAPA now carries a **severity-defaulted, editable `target_completion_date`** (Critical 30 / Major 60 / Minor 90 calendar days from raise — a `domain/capa/targets.py` code constant, set at BOTH `Capa(...)` construction sites: `build_capa` [direct-raise + the NC→CAPA auto-link + risk-spawn] and the inline `spawn_capa_from_complaint`), and a **new daily Beat sweep** (`services/capa/overdue.py` + `tasks/capa.py::easysynq.capa.overdue_sweep`) notifies the seeded **"QMS Owner"** role when an open CAPA passes it. CAPAs have **no `Task` row** (only the action-plan *approval* spawns a task), so the escalation timer can't see them → this is a **task-less** sweep modeled on `fan_out_awareness` (fresh session per CAPA + `FOR UPDATE SKIP LOCKED` + an `overdue_notified_at` stamp = idempotent; `now_is_working`-gated), reusing `enqueue_awareness_one` + `resolve_subject("CAPA", …)` (which already loads the CAPA identifier/title from `documented_information` + deep-links `/capa?capa={id}`). A `PATCH /capas/{id}` (gated by the existing **`capa.update`**, NO new key) sets/clears the date (409 on a terminal CAPA, clears the stamp to re-arm, emits a `CAPA_TARGET_DATE_SET` audit); the shared `_capa()` serializer gains `target_completion_date` + a **server-computed `overdue`** (`current_org_tz()`; false for terminal/null). A **backfill CLI** (`backfill_capa_target_dates.py`, idempotent, `--dry-run`) dates existing non-terminal CAPAs. The **FE** CAPA drawer gains a target-date row + a colour-safe Overdue `StatusBadge` + a process-scoped-permission-gated inline `type=date` edit. **Migration 0070:** 2 nullable `capa` columns (`target_completion_date` Date · `overdue_notified_at` timestamptz, ORM-mirrored or `alembic check` phantom-DROPs) + **2 additive `event_type` values** (`CAPA_OVERDUE` · `CAPA_TARGET_DATE_SET`, sourced from `EVENT_TYPE_VALUES`) + the **global** `capa.overdue` `notification_template` seed (no `org_id` → CI-covered; RESTRICT-FK-guarded downgrade). Also bundles **3 `.claude` automations** (the `notification-wiring-reviewer` agent, the `model-registration` PostToolUse hook, the `/new-notification-event` skill) as the first commit.

⚠ **The dedup discriminator is doubly load-bearing — two reviewers + Codex each caught a distinct silent-drop.** The sweep emits with `subject_version_id = uuid5(capa_id, target_date, rearm_seq)` against the awareness dedup index `uq_notification_dedup_awareness (recipient, event_key, subject_type, subject_id, subject_version_id) WHERE task_id IS NULL`. (1) The **date** component re-arms a future-extend (a new date → a new key → fires; mutation-verified). (2) `rearm_seq` = **COUNT of `CAPA_TARGET_DATE_SET` audits** for the CAPA (a no-migration monotonic re-arm version) was added for the **Codex** clear→reset-to-the-SAME-date case: without it a date cleared then re-set to the identical value reuses the old key → the index dedupes the resend → `_process_one` stamps it (Option Y) → the re-armed overdue silently never sends. Idempotency holds (the CAPA is locked `FOR UPDATE` during the sweep → `rearm_seq` is stable mid-txn). ⚠ **The `notification-wiring-reviewer` (dogfooded — this slice's OWN new agent) caught an R4-1 CRITICAL the opus reviewer undersold:** the `CAPA_OVERDUE` audit was written unconditionally → a FALSE audit on a no-recipient sweep AND a DUPLICATE WORM audit on an all-deduped re-arm → fixed by guarding `session.add(AuditEvent)` behind `if created > 0` (the escalation `if created_ids:` precedent). ⚠ **The diff-critic caught a claim⇄fire asymmetry the opus reviewer missed:** `_process_one`'s locked re-check omitted the claim's `target_completion_date < today`, so a `PATCH` that extends a claimed-overdue CAPA to the FUTURE (clearing the stamp) in the claim→lock gap would fire-and-stamp a **non-overdue** CAPA → the genuine future overdue then never re-claims (silent drop) → fixed by re-asserting `target < today` in the locked WHERE + threading `today` in. ⚠ **The `web-test-trap-reviewer` caught a MAJOR the web gate can't:** `CapaDrawer` is never unmounted (`opened={capaId!==null}`), so the date input's `useState` persisted across CAPA selections (a stale CAPA-A date savable against CAPA B) AND never seeded from the current value → fixed with a `useEffect` keyed on `[capaId, capa?.target_completion_date]`.

⚠ **Owner-decided: a no-valid-recipient sweep must NOT stamp → it retries.** The QMS Owner IS the floor; if the org has zero active holders the sweep leaves `overdue_notified_at` NULL so the overdue re-fires once a QM is assigned (compliance-safest, honors "must-not-silently-drop"; the rejected alternative — the escalation-style terminal-no-op stamp — would permanently lose the notice). The data-model choice (A1: one severity-defaulted editable `target_completion_date`, NOT per-stage SLAs) was owner-ratified.

⚠ **A pre-existing weekend-broken test the Saturday CI run exposed (folded in to unblock — NOT this slice's bug).** PR #302's first CI happened to run on **Saturday 2026-06-27** and `test_periodic_review.py::test_decide_changes_requested_keeps_clock_and_renag` failed — PROVEN pre-existing (fails identically at `b2b520f`, the branch base, in a review-sweep path this slice never touches; each CI shard spins its own testcontainer → no cross-shard pollution). Mechanism: `_due_released_doc` sets `next_review_due = today`; the re-nag task's `due_at = snap_to_working_day(today)` snaps **forward to Monday on a weekend** → the task isn't overdue → `REVIEW_OVERDUE` correctly doesn't fire → the test's "due_at in the past" premise breaks. Owner chose to fix it here: pin the test's `next_review_due` to a clearly-past date so the snapped `due_at` stays overdue any weekday (verified locally with the canonical tz on a Saturday: the whole file 15/15). ⚠ The "fails-locally-on-Friday-too" puzzle reconciled: `_canonical_tz()` was already on Saturday (early-AM UTC) while the system-local date showed Friday — so the weekend condition was active locally, letting the fix be verified without waiting for Monday. (The recurring **weekday-flaky-after-the-business-calendar** trap from `engineering-patterns`, confirmed live on CI.)

**Codex — 4 findings over 2 rounds, all real, all fixed, all threads replied.** (R1) `CapaTargetDate.target_completion_date = None` default → a `PATCH {}` (or a generated client omitting the field) silently cleared the deadline → made **required-but-nullable** (an explicit `null` still clears) + a `PATCH {}`→422 test + openapi `required`; the FE drawer's `can("capa.update")` used the SYSTEM-scope probe, hiding the editor from a process-linked CAPA's Process Owner (PROCESS-scoped grant) the PATCH would authorize → **process-scoped `usePermissions({level:"PROCESS",id:capa.process_id})`** mirroring `AdvancePanel`. (R2) the Save `onSuccess` blanked the controlled input → an UNCHANGED save left it blank → the next Save sent `null` (deadline clear) → dropped the clear (the `useEffect` keeps it synced); the same-date re-arm dedup-collapse (the `rearm_seq` fix above).

**Named-not-faked deferrals:** admin-editable severity offsets (the SLA-offset-editor residual generalized to CAPA) · process-owner / CAPA-raiser notification routing (QMS Owner is the only recipient; no clean process→owner resolver) · a CAPA-overdue **escalation tier** · per-stage SLA deadlines · `capa.overdue` in the daily digest rollup · two `PATCH`-test coverage gaps (a clear-to-null re-arm assertion; a terminal-CAPA `overdue:false` GET) · the backfill's per-CAPA (vs per-org) tz resolution (immaterial under single-org D1) · the carried Notification tail (working-calendar depth, escalate_3, the manager-graph writer, the P2 read-access gating, Option-B/C). **Test deltas:** api unit **1071→1078** (+7: `test_capa_overdue_model` 2 · `test_capa_targets` 2 · `test_notification_capa_overdue` 2 · `test_capa_overdue_task` 1), **+~14 integration** (sweep 6 · PATCH 6 · backfill 1 · a default-at-raise assertion in `test_capa.py`), web **1292→1300** (+8: the drawer field/badge/edit + permission gating + the unchanged-save + the reopen-reset regression). **Process:** brainstorm (owner: A1 severity-default editable · QMS-Owner recipient · BE+FE · 30/60/90 · backfill CLI) → spec → 8-task plan → subagent-driven (fresh implementer + spec+quality reviewer each; the migration via the **migration-reviewer** [CLEAN + an alembic round-trip] + a DB-only live-smoke [columns · 2 enum values · global template]) → final whole-branch (opus **Ready=With-fixes** + diff-critic, converged: the claim⇄fire Minor fixed) → `/pr` (all gates green) → CI (the Saturday pre-existing-test catch) → 2 Codex rounds (4 P2s, all fixed). (S-capa-overdue, BE+FE+CLI, migration **0070** [head `0069→0070`], NO new key [catalog 102, reuses `capa.update`], **2 new `event_type` values**, api unit 1071→1078, +~14 integration, web 1292→1300, PR #302 squash `bdd4fd5`.)

### S-escalate2 — a second (final) escalation tier (closes the named `escalate_2` residual; BE-only; migration **0069** [head `0068→0069`]; PR #300 squash `374c9ef`)

**What shipped — the deferred 2nd escalation tier.** When an escalation-enabled task stays unactioned to **+3 business days** past due, the timer sweep now fires a **distinct `task.escalated_final`** notification to the seeded **"Top Management"** role (migration 0038; resolved by `Role.name` via `users_with_roles`) → **QMS Owner floor** if Top Management has no valid recipient, reusing the existing per-task sweep end-to-end. The seam was reserved in code (the `_due_task_ids` docstring named `escalate_2` as "the next tier that must teach both the claim and `due_steps` together"). **`timer.py`** gains `TimerStep.ESCALATE_2` + `TimerPolicy.escalate_2_after`/`TimerStamps.escalated_2_at` (both `= None` defaults — frozen-dataclass-legal, last position — so escalate_2 stays inert until wired, which decoupled the build tasks and kept `escalation.py` valid between the timer-step task and the dispatch task) + a `due_steps` AFTER-direction branch (`now_is_working`-gated, reuses `business_threshold` unchanged, chronologically last). **`escalation.py`** gains: a 5th policy-aware `_due_task_ids` claim disjunct `(escalate_2_after IS NOT NULL & escalated_2_at IS NULL)` (a strict superset of `due_steps`' ESCALATE_2 firing condition → can only DELAY, never DROP; configured-offset-gated → no S-claim-filter re-claim churn); `resolve_escalation_2_recipients(session, task) -> (ids, via)`; the dispatch `else: # ESCALATE_1` split into `elif ESCALATE_1` (byte-identical body + a `"tier": 1` audit key) + a new `else: # ESCALATE_2` branch emitting `task.escalated_final` + a `TASK_ESCALATED` audit carrying `tier: 2`. **`constants.py`/`classes.py`** add `EVENT_TASK_ESCALATED_FINAL = "task.escalated_final"` + its `_TASK_EVENT_VARS` whitelist entry (⚠ omit it and the render silently drops all template vars — the S-remind2 trap) + CRITICAL class (pierces quiet hours, like `task.escalated`). **Migration 0069** (real DDL this time): `ADD COLUMN sla_policy.escalate_2_after Interval` + `task.escalated_2_at timestamptz` (both nullable, ORM-mirrored or `alembic check` phantom-DROPs); seeds the **global** `task.escalated_final` template (no `org_id` → CI-covered); `UPDATE sla_policy SET escalate_2_after = INTERVAL '3 days' WHERE escalate_2_after IS NULL AND escalate_1_after IS NOT NULL` — the **`escalate_1_after IS NOT NULL` carve-out keeps DOC_ACK/PERIODIC_REVIEW with no tier-2** (they never got tier-1); guarded downgrade (`NOT EXISTS(<notification>)` before the template delete, then `UPDATE … NULL`, then drop_column ×2). **Owner-ratified policy:** tier-2 recipient = Top Management → QMS floor (NO grand-manager walk — `app_user.manager_id` is unpopulated in practice, so even tier-1 always hits the QM fallback today; the manager-graph writer stays a deferral); +3 business days timing. **NO new permission key** (catalog 102), **NO WORM/authz/web/openapi/FE**.

⚠ **Two recurring traps re-surfaced.** (1) **Distinct event key is mandatory** — reusing `task.escalated` would collapse the 2nd escalation onto tier-1's row under the `(recipient_user_id, task_id, event_key)` dedup (the exact S-remind2 REMIND_2 bug), so `task.escalated_final` is load-bearing. (2) **The blast radius** — enabling `escalate_2_after` makes the claim disjunct live → the S-claim-filter "fully-fired escalate-enabled APPROVE" exclusion test now re-claims its task → fixed by stamping the **5th** step (`escalated_2_at=_STAMPED`); the **DOC_ACK** exclusion is untouched (carve-out keeps `escalate_2_after` NULL there). The existing tier-1 escalation tests at `_BASE = Wed 2026-06-24` do **NOT** fire tier-2 (the +3bd threshold = **Thu 06-25 > Wed**), so the audit "exactly one TASK_ESCALATED" tests stay green — confirmed by the whole-branch review walking every escalation test. The audit `"tier"` discriminator is **additive-safe** (the existing escalate_1 audit assertions are key-scoped via `ae.after.get(...)`, not whole-dict equality). ⚠ The `created_ids`/`exists_ids` locals in the ESCALATE_2 branch are intentionally bare `[]` (NOT re-annotated): they're already typed `list[uuid.UUID]` at the ESCALATE_1 branch, which pins the function-scope type — a second annotation would trip a mypy "already defined" error (a review Minor adjudicated non-actionable: the bare form is the mypy-correct one, mypy-strict passes).

⚠ **The final whole-branch review (opus + diff-critic, CONVERGED) caught one real defect the per-task reviews missed — a cross-shard test-isolation false-PASS the diff-critic EMPIRICALLY REPRODUCED.** `test_escalate_2_qm_fallback` asserted the QM floor resolves, but that only holds if the shared default org has zero "Top Management" holders — and three OTHER integration files (`test_capa` / `test_leadership_authorization` / `test_improvement_authorization`) leak un-cleaned SYSTEM-scoped Top Management assignments into that same oldest-org (`users_with_roles` counts them — it excludes only `managed_by`-scoped grants). Green only by shard luck; `pytest test_capa::…two_tier_approval test_escalate_2_qm_fallback` reproduced the `0==1` failure. Fixed by self-providing the precondition (delete leaked Top Management assignments at the test's start; the within-file `to_top_management` test already cleans its own assignment in a `finally`). ⚠ **Codex round 1 (2 findings): P1 fixed, P2 owner-deferred.** **P1** (`resolve_escalation_2_recipients`'s `if top:` returned non-empty-but-all-invalid Top Management ids → the dispatch loop dropped them via `_recipient_for_user` → `attempted==0` → terminal `escalated_2_at` stamp → the **final escalation silently dropped** even with an active QMS Owner) was REAL and FIXED (commit `75b24e3`): fall to the QM floor on **"no VALID Top Management recipient"** (not merely "empty role"), mirroring the tier-1 manager→QM fallthrough on an invalid manager, + a mutation-distinguishing test (`test_escalate_2_falls_to_qm_when_top_management_inactive` — LOCKED-only TM + active QM → `via=qm_fallback`; RED on old / GREEN on new). **P2** (Top Management holds only `capa.read` per 0038, so a non-CAPA tier-2 reveals subject id/title + an unopenable link) is REAL but **owner-deferred as a v1.x residual**: it mirrors tier-1 exactly (`task.escalated` carries the same `_TASK_EVENT_VARS` to the assignee's manager, who can equally lack read), the recipient was a deliberate design choice, single-org governance (D1) makes leadership *awareness* of a stuck task the intent, and the "proper" content/recipient gating is cross-cutting (it changes tier-1 too) + a policy call. Both Codex threads got substantive replies; Codex 👍 after the fix.

**Named-not-faked deferrals:** the **P2 read-access gating** (cross-cutting "gate escalation recipients/content on per-subject read access" — changes tier-1 too; a v1.x slice + policy decision) · **escalate_3** · the **manager-graph writer** (no path populates `app_user.manager_id` → grand-manager resolution is dead, intentionally skipped) · the SLA-offset admin editor (`sla_policy` stays seed-only / SELECT-only for the app role) · the carried **Option-B** index narrowing + **Option-C** pre-due threshold-gate (from S-claim-filter) · **capa.overdue** · **working-calendar depth**. ⚠ **Dev-env learning (now in `docs/dev-workflow.md`):** the FULL `-m integration` suite run in ONE process / ONE shared DB on this box yields ~54 FALSE failures — environmental (`pg_dump` is only in the worker image, not on the host → backup/restore drills fail `pg_dump not found`) + the documented single-DB `Organization.scalar_one()` / mirror cross-file pollution — with ZERO failures in the slice's own domain; the valid local proof is the SCOPED file/`-k` run + a targeted cross-file ordering proof, and CI's 4 ISOLATED integration shards are authoritative (all green; 743 passed / 54 env+pollution fails locally). **Test deltas:** api unit **1063→1071** (+8: 6 `timer.py` ESCALATE_2 cases [ordering/threshold/stamp-gating/null-offset/now_is_working] + 2 `classes.py`/whitelist), **+4 integration** (`test_due_task_ids_claims_pending_escalate2` · `test_escalate_2_to_top_management` · `test_escalate_2_qm_fallback` · `test_escalate_2_falls_to_qm_when_top_management_inactive`), web **1292** unchanged. **Process:** brainstorm (owner chose escalate_2 over capa.overdue once the CAPA-has-no-due-date-model cost surfaced; tier-2 = Top Management → QMS floor; +3bd) → spec → 6-task plan → subagent-driven (fresh implementer + spec+quality reviewer each; the migration via the specialized **migration-reviewer** — CLEAN [13/13 traps] + an alembic round-trip + `check` clean; a seed live-smoke on a throwaway PG16 confirmed the carve-out [`escalate_2_after = 3 days` for the 10 escalate-enabled types, NULL for DOC_ACK/PERIODIC_REVIEW] + a clean guarded downgrade) → final whole-branch (opus + diff-critic, converged; the qm_fallback isolation defect fixed + proven) → `/pr` (ruff · `mypy src` 412 · unit 1071 · web 1292) → CI green (all 4 integration shards) → Codex round 1 (P1 fixed `75b24e3`, P2 deferred; CI re-green, Codex 👍) → squash-merge. (S-escalate2, BE-only, migration **0069** [head `0068→0069`], NO new key [catalog 102], api unit 1063→1071, +4 integration, web 1292, PR #300 squash `374c9ef`.)

### S-remind2 — a distinct second (final) reminder (re-introduces the S-notify-4-deferred 2nd reminder; BE-only; migration **0068** [head `0067→0068`]; PR #298 squash `e5b0d13`)

**What shipped — the deferred 2nd pre-due reminder, re-introduced.** S-notify-4 specced two reminders but shipped one: both REMIND_1 and REMIND_2 emitted under `task.due_soon`, and the in-app dedup (the partial-unique `(recipient_user_id, task_id, event_key) WHERE task_id IS NOT NULL` behind `_enqueue_one`'s `ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING`) **collapsed REMIND_2 onto REMIND_1's row** → it delivered nothing (the S-notify-4 final review caught the false-PASS where the test pre-stamped REMIND_2). Fix = a **distinct event key `task.due_final`** for REMIND_2: `constants.py` adds `EVENT_TASK_DUE_FINAL` + its `_TASK_EVENT_VARS` whitelist entry (without the whitelist entry the render silently drops the template variables — a broken-but-present notification a count test would still pass); `classes.py` maps it `ACTION_REQUIRED` (NOT CRITICAL — a *pre-due* reminder must not pierce quiet hours the way `task.overdue`/`task.escalated` do); `escalation.py`'s REMIND branch selects `EVENT_TASK_DUE_SOON if step is REMIND_1 else EVENT_TASK_DUE_FINAL` (the ONLY reminder emit site in `src/`; OVERDUE/ESCALATE branches + stamping/audit/recipients byte-identical). **Migration 0068** (NO DDL → `alembic check` trivially clean, ORM unchanged) seeds the **global** `task.due_final` template (the `notification_template` table has no `org_id` → the seed is CI-covered) and runs `UPDATE sla_policy SET remind_2_before = INTERVAL '1 day' WHERE remind_2_before IS NULL` (all 12 task types — a **final reminder 1 business day before due**); downgrade nulls `remind_2_before` and deletes the template **guarded by `NOT EXISTS (a notification referencing it)`** (the `notification.template_id` RESTRICT FK / S-notify-4 populated-DB-abort lesson). **`_due_task_ids` + `due_steps` need NO change** — S-claim-filter pre-activated the policy-gated remind_2 claim disjunct, so making `remind_2_before` non-NULL re-activates the second reminder with **zero claim/timer code change** (the seam landed exactly as designed). **NO new permission key** (catalog 102), **NO WORM/authz/web/openapi/FE** (the SPA renders the stored title/body + the notification *class* — it does not switch on `event_key`).

⚠ **The hidden blast radius — enabling `remind_2_before` makes REMIND_2 newly-live for EVERY task in `test_notification_timer_sweep.py` that leaves `remind_2_sent_at` NULL and whose `now ≥ due − 1bd`.** The two S-claim-filter exclusion tests' "fully-fired" tasks left `remind_2_sent_at` NULL → the now-live remind_2 claim disjunct re-claims them → `assert ... not in ids` would FLIP; fixed by adding `remind_2_sent_at=_STAMPED` (the **DOC_ACK** exclusion stays mutation-distinguishing via the still-live escalate tautology `escalated_1_at IS NULL`; the **APPROVE** one becomes a plain fully-fired guard — post-remind2 there's no APPROVE tautology left). The two escalation/doc-ack tests that leave remind_2 unstamped are **additive-safe** (their assertions are scoped to `task.escalated` — a new `task.due_final` to the assignee doesn't touch them) but were given `remind_2_sent_at=_STAMPED` to restore true isolation. The final whole-branch review (opus senior + diff-critic, **converged**) walked **all 24** timer tests and confirmed the audit COMPLETE (no other test breaks or false-passes; no test asserts a global `summary["steps"]`). ⚠ **Now-stale "remind_2 is inert" prose corrected:** the S-claim-filter `_due_task_ids` docstring + several test comments described remind_2 as inert / `remind_2_before=None`-for-all-types — false after 0068; reworded (the remind_2 disjunct is now the live second-reminder claim). **Named-not-faked deferrals:** escalate_2; an admin editor for the SLA offsets (`sla_policy` stays seed-only / SELECT-only for the app role); the **no-runtime-`sla_policy`-seeder new-org gap** — the only seeder is the 0065 migration (runs for orgs existing at migration time; 0002 creates the `DEFAULT` org so it is covered), so a brand-new org created *after* a migration gets no policies at all (single-org D1 makes it moot); the Option-B/Option-C residuals carried from S-claim-filter; the carried Notification tail (capa.overdue · working-calendar depth). **Test deltas:** api unit **1062→1063** (+1 `test_due_final_is_action_required`; `due_steps` REMIND_2 was already covered), **+1 integration** (`test_remind_2_distinct_final_reminder` — one sweep → two *distinct* notifications, mutation-distinguishing vs the old shared-key collapse), web **1292** unchanged. **Process:** brainstorm (residual menu → owner chose remind_2 + the 1-business-day cadence) → spec → 3-task plan → subagent-driven (per-task spec+quality review; the migration via the specialized **migration-reviewer** — CLEAN, confirmed the `sla_policy` UPDATE IS CI-covered via 0002-`DEFAULT`-org→0065-seed→0068, the guarded downgrade, idempotent DML, no-DDL `alembic check`) → final whole-branch (opus **Ready=Yes** + diff-critic **CLEAN** [re-run after a 600s infra-stall], converged, 24-test audit) → Minor fix wave (the stale-inert prose) → `/pr` (ruff · `mypy src` 412 · `pytest -m unit` 1063) → CI green (all 4 integration shards + the `migrations` round-trip). ⚠ **DOCKER IS AVAILABLE on this Linux box** — the whole-session "Docker-less box" framing was WRONG (it came from the session-start env note and was never verified; `docker 29.6.0` + compose are installed). The agent's shell user (`cojoa13`) was added to the `docker` group (`usermod -aG`) but an already-running login shell doesn't pick up the new group → **wrap docker-needing commands in `sg docker -c "…"`** (it re-reads `/etc/group`; a fresh login works directly). This unlocked the **LOCAL** proofs CI used to own: `-m integration` (the timer file ran **26 passed** on a real PG16 testcontainer — the two-distinct-notifications proof end-to-end) + a real-stack **migration live-smoke** — `alembic 0067→0068→0067` on the **populated AHT DB** (role `easysynq`) set all 12 `sla_policy` rows to `remind_2_before=1 day` + seeded the `task.due_final` template (correct title/subject), and the downgrade cleanly reverted (the guarded template delete on real data), leaving the stack pristine (deliberately NO live sweep — it would fire real reminders/emails to actual users). See `docs/dev-workflow.md` for the durable `sg docker` note. (S-remind2, BE-only, migration **0068** [head `0067→0068`], NO new key [catalog 102], api unit 1062→1063, +1 integration, web 1292 unchanged, PR #298 squash `e5b0d13`.)

### S-claim-filter — policy-aware timer-sweep claim (the recurring "claim-threshold filter" Codex P2 close-out, **Option A**; BE-only; NO migration [head stays `0067`]; PR #296 squash `3be2716`)

**What shipped — the deferred `_due_task_ids` claim tautology, CLOSED.** The escalation `timer_sweep`'s coarse pre-filter `services/notifications/escalation.py::_due_task_ids` OR-ed four stamp-NULL clauses, two of which are **tautologies** given the migration-0065 seed: `remind_2_sent_at IS NULL` (always true — `remind_2_before=None` for every seeded `sla_policy`, so `timer.due_steps` never fires/stamps REMIND_2) and, for **DOC_ACK / PERIODIC_REVIEW**, `escalated_1_at IS NULL` (`escalate_1_after=None`). So every open task with an active policy + a `due_at` was re-claimed on **every** 5-minute sweep, *forever* — each re-claim running the full `process_task_timers` no-op (advisory lock → `FOR UPDATE SKIP LOCKED` SELECT → policy SELECT → instance GET → calendar resolve → commit) only for `due_steps` to return `[]`. Bounded but the dominant per-sweep cost, growing linearly with the open-task count (sharpened by the S-notify-4 live-smoke). **The fix (query-only):** make the claim **policy-aware** — gate each stamp-NULL on its `SlaPolicy` offset being configured (non-NULL), mirroring `due_steps`' own `policy.<offset> is not None and stamp is None` gating: `(remind_1_before IS NOT NULL ∧ remind_1_sent_at IS NULL) | (remind_2_before IS NOT NULL ∧ remind_2_sent_at IS NULL) | (overdue_notified_at IS NULL) | (escalate_1_after IS NOT NULL ∧ escalated_1_at IS NULL)`. **OVERDUE keeps a stamp-only gate** (no SLA offset — it fires at `due_at`, matching `due_steps`). **remind_2 is kept policy-gated and INERT** (not deleted) — `remind_2_before IS NOT NULL` is false for every seeded policy, so the disjunct is provably never satisfiable today (NOT a tautology, unlike the old bare clause); the future "distinct remind_2" slice just flips the seed with **zero** claim change. A fully-fired task now evaluates all four disjuncts to false → not claimed; the permanent re-claim is gone. **NO migration** (head stays `0067`), **NO new permission key** (catalog 102), **NO WORM/authz/web/openapi change**; `due_steps`/`process_task_timers`/stamping/audit/recipients are **byte-identical** — only the pre-filter tightens.

⚠ **The claim only ever gets TIGHTER, never looser — proven both directions by the final whole-branch review.** The opus senior reviewer + `diff-critic` **independently converged** that the new predicate is a **strict subset of the old claim** AND a **superset of `due_steps`' firing condition** (every `due_steps` firing predicate is `<claim-disjunct> ∧ now_is_working ∧ now ≥ threshold`; the claim drops only the time conjuncts), so it can only ever *delay* a task to the next sweep, never drop or mis-fire a real notification — the only newly-excluded tasks are the fully-fired/inert ones `due_steps` already returns `[]` for. ⚠ **Option B (narrow `ix_task_timer_pending` to match) was evaluated and DROPPED, not faked:** the precise claim is a *join* qual (it references `sla_policy`), so the planner can't push it into the `task` baserel scan — a stamp-disjunction partial index would be **rejected** (a net regression to seqscan) unless a redundant task-only baserel predicate `(remind_1_sent_at IS NULL OR overdue_notified_at IS NULL OR escalated_1_at IS NULL)` is *also* added to the query; even then its only marginal benefit over A is a smaller single claim-scan (A already removes the dominant per-task no-op loop), so it isn't worth a migration. ⚠ **Named residuals (not faked):** the **pre-due claim churn** — a not-yet-overdue task still matches `overdue_notified_at IS NULL` (it genuinely has a pending OVERDUE step) and is claimed each sweep until OVERDUE fires; eliminating *that* is the deferred conservative-**threshold-gate** (Option C — business-day thresholds aren't exactly SQL-expressible, so it needs a provably-conservative padded lower bound + a fudge constant) · the Option-B index narrowing · distinct remind_2 · escalate_2 · capa.overdue · working-calendar depth (multiple named calendars/org, holiday recurrence). **Tests (all integration, `test_notification_timer_sweep.py`):** two **mutation-distinguishing** exclusion cases — a fully-fired open APPROVE task (the headline remind_2 tautology) and a fully-fired open DOC_ACK task (the remind_2 + escalate tautologies) must **not** be claimed (RED on the old 4-way claim, GREEN after the policy-aware predicate); plus a four-part over-tightening guard — pending remind_1/overdue/escalate (APPROVE) **and** a pending-overdue DOC_ACK (a `diff-critic` Minor folded in — proves the DOC_ACK policy JOIN resolves, so the DOC_ACK *exclusion* test can't silently pass-for-wrong-reason if the seed ever drops DOC_ACK's policy) must still be claimed. All assertions are **run-scoped membership** on **open-state** tasks (a DONE task is excluded by `state.in_(_OPEN)` regardless → wouldn't distinguish the mutation); no shared-DB pollution (reuses the default org — no 2nd `Organization`, the S-notify-4 `test_restore` `scalar_one` trap avoided). Process: brainstorm (owner chose A over A+B/C after the planner subtlety surfaced) → spec → 2-task plan → subagent-driven (each task implement → spec+quality review, both ✅) → final whole-branch (opus senior **Ready=Yes** + diff-critic **CLEAN**, converged; 2 Minors — loose positive-control comments + the DOC_ACK join control — folded) → green local gate (ruff · `mypy src` 412 files · `pytest -m unit` 1062 passed) → `/pr` → **all CI green incl. all 4 integration shards** (the authoritative run of the 3 new tests — the Docker-less dev box can't run integration locally). (S-claim-filter, BE-only, NO migration [head stays `0067`], NO new key [catalog 102], api unit 1062 unchanged, +3 integration, web 1292 unchanged, PR #296 squash `3be2716`; final review opus+diff-critic CLEAN/converged, 2 Minors folded.)

### S-orgtz-unify — unify the org timezone onto the working calendar (the env-vs-DB tz cross-cutting close-out, **R56**; BE+CLI+docs; NO migration [head stays `0067`]; PR #294 squash `0008b08`)

**What shipped — the named "unify `_org_tz()` onto the calendar" residual + R29's D-3 divergence, CLOSED.** Three org-tz sources had drifted: env `easysynq_org_timezone` (→ `review._org_tz()`, sync/session-free) drove `next_review_due` + the `review_state` badge + the mgmt-review cadence + the `_document` serializer; `organization.timezone` (R8 effective-date authoritative) seeded the calendar; `working_calendar.timezone` (R29/R55 timer-canonical, editable via S-notify-7) drove snap/timer. On any non-UTC org the **review/cadence frame (env) and the snap/timer frame (DB calendar) diverged** (the accepted R55 D-3 "badge leads the working-day notification" + the `_fmt_date` render mismatch). This slice collapses them to **ONE canonical, DB-resolved tz**. New `services/common/org_clock.py`: `resolve_org_tz(session, org_id)` = the fail-safe chain **`is_default working_calendar.timezone → organization.timezone → env → UTC`** + a pure `pick_tz` + a request/sweep-scoped `ContextVar` (`current_org_tz` / `set_request_org_tz` [no reset — per-request asyncio-task isolation] / `using_org_tz` [reset CM]). `resolve_working_calendar` (escalation.py) sources its tz from the SAME `pick_tz` → **parity by construction** (calendar/timer frame ≡ review/date frame). **Hybrid mechanism (D-2):** `today_org()` is contextvar-backed — set at the auth boundary (`get_current_user`, the universal boundary since `require()` routes through it) + wrapped around every WORKER render; the genuine date-*transform* functions (`compute_next_review_due`, `read_cadence`, `_last_released_effective_from`) take an **explicit `org_tz`** (pure, unit-testable). **R8 cutover stays UTC** (D-4 — only date display/derivation moves to the canonical tz). Folded in: `_fmt_date` re-converts an aware datetime to `current_org_tz()` before `.date()`; **OVERDUE is now `now_is_working`-gated** (closes R55 D-5's weekend-pierce exemption — a weekend/holiday overdue notice defers to the next working day, doc 10 §9.5); `cli/backfill_review_dates.py` recomputes stored `next_review_due` into the canonical tz (idempotent, `--dry-run`; MR next-due is DERIVED → no backfill). **NO migration** (head stays `0067`), **NO new permission key** (catalog 102), **NO web/FE change** (`review_state`/MR badge are server-computed — values just get more correct), env var KEPT as the bottom fallback, `organization.timezone` & `working_calendar.timezone` stay independently editable (NO S-notify-7 regression). New register **R56** + amend-notes on R8 & R55.

⚠ **THE crux the final whole-branch review (opus + diff-critic CONVERGED) caught — a load-bearing false-PASS the per-task gates + the local `mypy`/targeted-unit gates ALL missed:** the §3.2.2 `using_org_tz` wrap was DROPPED on the WORKER paths. Three sweeps (`sweep_reviews`, `sweep_mgmt_reviews`, the ack `sweep_acks`) enqueue the `task.assigned` "Due by: {{task.due_at|date}}" template with the contextvar UNSET → `_fmt_date` reframed the `snap_to_working_day`-produced **cal.tz-aware** `due_at` to the previous UTC day (**REGRESSING the Codex #291 P2 fix** — pre-slice `_fmt_date` did a bare `.date()` on the cal.tz object = correct), AND `_cutover` computed the STORED `next_review_due` via `current_org_tz()` — unset in the `release_due` Beat → env/UTC. **ALL east-of-UTC-only → masked on the dev Chicago org (west) + CI (UTC)** = ships green. Fix (in-PR): wrap each worker enqueue in `using_org_tz(cal.tz)` (mirror the escalation sweep, already wrapped); `_cutover` resolves `resolve_org_tz(session, doc.org_id)` EXPLICITLY (fixes both the request `release()` AND the Beat). `engine.py:222` (skips DOC_ACK/PERIODIC_REVIEW, request-context for the rest), `spawn.py:114` (request), `service.py:88` (request) correctly need no wrap. diff-critic also caught the ack site opus missed.

⚠ **Two MORE issues surfaced AFTER the local gate — both why running the FULL suite before the PR is load-bearing:** (a) the full `-m unit` (run by `/pr`, NOT my targeted per-task suites) caught a PRE-EXISTING Codex #291 test (`test_duedate_snap.py::test_snapped_value_renders_calendar_date_not_utc`) that calls `_fmt_date` DIRECTLY with no contextvar — the §3.4 change made it re-convert to UTC → wrap it in `using_org_tz(tokyo)` to model the (now-wrapped) production render. (b) CI's integration shard caught a date-math bug in the new sweep-render verification test — `(7 - isoweekday()) % 7` targets the next **SUNDAY** (weekday 7), not Monday; it set `next_review_due` to a Sunday, the sweep correctly **SNAPPED** `due_at` forward to Monday, and the test asserted the unsnapped Sunday → `(1 - isoweekday()) % 7` for a real Monday. **The CI run PROVED the production fix correct** (the body rendered the Tokyo Monday `2026-06-29`, not the UTC Sunday); both fixes were TEST-ONLY, production code untouched.

⚠ **Other load-bearing notes:** a `ContextVar.set()` in an `async` FastAPI dependency propagates to the handler/serializers (same task) + no reset needed (per-request task isolation, the `request_id_var` precedent) — but a WORKER (multi-org sweep) MUST use `using_org_tz` (reset) so it can't leak across tasks. The HTTP propagation integration test is only mutation-distinguishing ~14/24h (the UTC-vs-cal "today" straddle) → backstopped by a deterministic monkeypatched `get_current_user` unit test. The OVERDUE gate reversal broke 3 existing weekend/holiday-OVERDUE unit tests (asserted `[OVERDUE]` on a Sat/holiday → now `[]`) — updated to the new gated semantics. CI `mypy` is `mypy src` (does NOT check tests). The ruff `--fix` PostToolUse hook repeatedly stripped just-added imports before their usage landed (F401→F821) — add the using code first. **Named residuals (not faked):** the 5 ship-as-is review Minors [`resolve_org_tz` docstring "never raises" is aspirational (DB I/O propagates); the propagation test doesn't restore `set_approver_release` (matches precedent); `test_date_filter_formats_datetime` now implicitly relies on the UTC default; no `--dry-run`=True backfill test; the backfill test asserts `!=wrong` not `==target` (idempotency covers it)] · the mutation-verify (`resolve_org_tz`→UTC) is CI/live-smoke-authoritative · the R55 "Named residuals" prose still names the old D-5 exemption (superseded by the appended R56 amend-note, per the append-don't-rewrite convention). Process: brainstorm (owner: cal-canonical-with-fallback + hybrid mechanism + all 3 scope adds) → spec → 10-task plan → subagent-driven (fresh implementer + task-reviewer each, per-task fixes folded) → final whole-branch (opus + diff-critic, 1 root cause / 4 sites, fixed) → green local gate → PR → `/pr` full-`-m unit` caught (a) → CI integration caught (b). (S-orgtz-unify, BE+CLI+docs, NO migration [head stays `0067`], NO new key [catalog 102], api unit 1052→1062 [+~12 incl. the new `test_org_clock`], +5 integration, web 1292 unchanged, PR #294 squash `0008b08`; final review 1 root-cause/4 sites + 2 post-gate test fixes.)

### S-duedate-snap — snap a task's `due_at` to a working day at materialize (R29 weekend-OVERDUE close-out, **R55**; BE-only; NO migration [head stays `0067`]; PR #291 squash `f879395`)

**What shipped — the un-numbered residual S-notify-6 AND S-notify-7 both deferred.** S-notify-6 wired `working_calendar` into the timer **OFFSETS** (reminders/escalation skip weekends) but KEPT **OVERDUE raw** (`now >= due_at`) because the root cause is upstream: `due_at` itself is raw wall-clock (`engine._due_at` = `now()+timedelta(hours=…)`; seeded `default_sla={'hours':120}` = 120 clock-hours) and frequently lands on a weekend → an unshifted OVERDUE fires `task.overdue` (escalation-class, quiet-hours-pierce-eligible) on a Saturday, which **doc 10 §9.5 forbids**. This slice **numbers it R55** and fixes it **at the source**: when a `Task.due_at` is materialized, if its date (in the calendar's tz) is a **non-working day** it is snapped **FORWARD to the next working day, preserving local time-of-day**; a working-day `due_at` is unchanged. So OVERDUE + every business-day offset land on a working day **with no OVERDUE special-casing in `due_steps`** (the timer is behaviorally unchanged). **NO migration** (head stays `0067`), **NO new permission key** (engine logic, R38, catalog stays 102), **NO web/openapi**, **NO WORM/authz/signature_event touch** (this only changes a `Task.due_at` value).

**The five materialize sites (exhaustive — grep-confirmed by 2 reviewers).** A pure `services/notifications/timer.py::snap_to_working_day(due_at, cal)` (forward-only · idempotent · the returned instant's cal.tz date is ALWAYS a working day [a spring-forward midnight-gap can normalize the reconstructed wall time ACROSS midnight onto a non-working day → each candidate is **RE-CHECKED** on the resolved instant, the IDEM-1 fix] · exhaustion **fail-safe returns the input UNCHANGED**, never a never-overdue far-future sentinel = fail-OPEN) + a tiny seam `services/notifications/duedate.py` (`resolve_calendar`/`snap_due_at`, **lazy-imports** `resolve_working_calendar` to avoid the `escalation→workflow.__init__→engine` cycle — load-bearing). **INSTANT sites** (a true instant, no calendar-day intent — just snap in cal.tz): `workflow/engine.py::_materialize_stage` (every engine-materialized task; the single chokepoint for instantiate AND stage-advance) + the DOC_ACK sweep override (`ack/sweep.py`, a NEW `snapped_due_at` local fed to BOTH the `update(Task)` AND the `due_at_override` — never reassign the org-spanning loop-invariant). **DATE-anchored sites** (D-5): `vault/review.py` (PERIODIC_REVIEW), `mgmt_review/spawn.py` (MR_ACTION, `_action_due_at` now takes `cal`), `mgmt_review/cadence.py` (MR_INPUT) now resolve the calendar FIRST and **build `due_at` at midnight in `cal.tz`** (not the env `easysynq_org_timezone`), then snap. `workflow/service.py::instantiate_approval` correctly has **no `due_at`** (NULL → excluded by the timer's `due_at IS NOT NULL` claim) → NOT a site.

**Owner decisions (AskUserQuestion ×5, ratified 2026-06-25).** D-1 R55/forward-only/preserve-time · D-2 all 5 sites (every `TaskType` has a seeded `SlaPolicy` → any can fire a weekend OVERDUE) · D-3 snap the PERIODIC_REVIEW **task** due_at + **accept the `review_state` badge divergence** (stored `next_review_due` UNCHANGED) · D-4 new-only, **NO backfill** · **D-5 (surfaced by spec-validation TZ-1):** the 3 date-anchored sites build in `cal.tz` so build+snap+timer share ONE business-day frame (the S-notify-7 "the calendar owns the business-day tz" authority) — **zero behavior change** under a correctly-configured deployment (env tz == calendar tz). ⚠ **The crux the 6-lens pre-code spec-validation (19 agents, ~2.3M tok, 7 confirmed findings ALL folded) caught: TZ-1 (MAJOR)** — the 3 date-anchored sites built `due_at` in the **env** `easysynq_org_timezone` (default UTC) while the snap/timer judge in the **DB** `working_calendar.timezone` (the dev box already diverges: env UTC, cal America/Chicago) → under divergence the snap re-judged an operator's date in the wrong frame (could push an operator-set Monday to Tuesday); resolved by D-5. **IDEM-1** — the DST-gap re-check (empirically reproduced on America/Nuuk 2024-03-29: a Saturday 23:30 candidate normalizes to a non-working Sunday). Both MAJOR/real, both fixed pre-code.

**Reconcile (the heart — why the timer needs no change + no double-shift):** `business_threshold` computes offsets FROM `due_at`; with `due_at` already a working day, REMIND/ESCALATE/OVERDUE all land on working days — nothing snaps twice (`business_threshold` still receives ONE `due_at`, now already a working day). The S-notify-6 offset tests are unaffected (`due_steps` byte-unchanged; only a new pure helper is ADDED to `timer.py`). The escalation/reminder timings re-anchor to the real (working-day) due date (never earlier than the §9.5 intent — benign, documented).

⚠ **Build traps.** The PostToolUse ruff `--fix` strips a just-added import if the using code isn't present yet (F401) — re-added at spawn.py/cadence.py/the periodic test after the usage landed (the engineering-patterns trap). ⚠ **Shared-DB test design:** the session DB's default-org calendar tz is unpredictable across files (a throwaway org with a committed calendar can't be cleaned — REVOKE DELETE / the S-notify-4/7 leaked-org trap that breaks `test_restore`'s `scalar_one`) → every integration assertion RESOLVES the org's **actual** calendar and checks against `snap_to_working_day(raw, cal)` + `is_working_day(...)` (robust + mutation-distinguishing). The pre-existing `test_periodic_review.py:301` exact-`due_at` assert was de-flaked the same way (RECON-1 sites). The MR `2026-12-31` assertion stays green (a Thursday → snap no-op; cal.tz==UTC seed) — a reviewer-noted latent coupling left as-is (no near-term risk; both reviewers rated "no action required").

**Process.** spec-first → 6-lens adversarial spec-validation (ultracode Workflow) → plan → 3-stage TDD build (pure helper+seam → wire 5 sites → integration+e2e) → **mutation-verified** (neutering `snap_to_working_day` fails 8 unit + all 3 key integration tests) → 2-lens whole-branch review (diff-critic **CLEAN** · whole-branch **READY**, 120 integration tests run live) → **live-smoke** (BE-only, deployed-worker snippets: AHT calendar resolved live = Mon-Fri/Chicago; `snap_due_at` Sat→Mon in cal.tz [time-of-day preserved]; D-5 `_action_due_at(Sat, cal)` built at Mon **00:00 Chicago**; a real `timer_sweep()`→`{tasks:0,steps:0}` clean; the deployed `due_steps` proved OLD raw-Sat OVERDUE-at-Sunday=True [the bug] vs NEW snapped OVERDUE-at-Sunday=False / at-Monday=True [fixed, on a working day]).

⚠ **Codex round 1 — 1 P2 (genuine, fixed `snap_to_working_day` to RETURN in `cal.tz`).** For an **east-of-UTC** calendar a date-anchored due that snaps to local Monday midnight returned as `Sun 15:00 UTC`; the notification renderer `notifications/render._fmt_date` formats `value.date()` at ENQUEUE (dispatch.py:163) without re-converting → the email showed **Sunday** for a Monday-due task (undercutting the slice's intent; the dev org Chicago/west-of-UTC was unaffected). Fix = return the snapped instant **in `cal.tz`** (the INSTANT is unchanged → persistence/`now`-comparisons unaffected; only the in-memory `.date()` render aligns); the working-day branch already returned the cal.tz-built input for date-anchored sites. Locked by a mutation-distinguishing unit test (`out.date()` is the Monday *local* date + `_fmt_date(out) == "2026-06-29"`, both fail on a UTC return). The broader `_fmt_date`-renders-UTC-`.date()` issue for an UNSNAPPED instant-site due on a non-UTC org is pre-existing (folds into the deferred `_org_tz()`-unification slice).

**Named residuals (not faked):** OVERDUE can still fire on a non-working day in two narrow edges — a sweep delayed across a working→non-working boundary (OVERDUE has no `now_is_working` gate, the ratified D-5 weekend-pierce exemption) + a post-materialize `working_calendar` edit (S-notify-7) turning an already-due date into a holiday · the env `easysynq_org_timezone` vs DB `working_calendar.timezone` remain two **un-unified** org-tz sources (unifying `_org_tz()` onto the calendar — which also fixes `_fmt_date` for unsnapped non-UTC due dates — is a deferred cross-cutting slice) · the `test_mgmt_review.py` UTC-coupling hardening · no backfill of existing open tasks · the carried Notification tail (claim-threshold-filter tautology · distinct `remind_2` · `escalate_2` · `capa.overdue` · multiple named calendars/org · holiday recurrence/bulk-import). **Tests:** api unit **1037→1052** (+15: weekend/holiday/idempotent/monotonic snaps · eastward+westward tz · the Nuuk midnight-DST-gap · exhaustion fail-safe · `_action_due_at` build-in-cal.tz [D-5 lock] · the cal.tz-return render lock [Codex P2]); **+3 integration** (the seam resolve+snap · the engine materialize e2e · a dedicated PERIODIC_REVIEW weekend-review snap [next_review_due unchanged, D-3]) + the de-flaked existing periodic assert; web unchanged (**1292**). (S-duedate-snap, BE-only, NO migration [head stays `0067`], NO new key [catalog 102], **R55**, api unit 1037→1052 +3 integration, web 1292, PR #291 squash `f879395`; spec-validation 7 findings folded · diff-critic+whole-branch CLEAN · Codex 1 round / 1 P2 fixed.)

### S-notify-7 — the `working_calendar` admin editor: make the business-day calendar configurable (R29 editor residual close-out; BE+FE; NO migration [head stays `0067`]; PR #289 squash `03419ce`)

**What shipped — the last R29 residual.** S-notify-6 wired `working_calendar` into the `timer_sweep` but left it **frozen at the Mon-Fri/`[]`/`<org-tz>` seed** — no in-app way to set the working days, add a holiday, rename it, or fix its timezone. This slice adds a **`config.update`-gated admin editor** for the org's **default** calendar, in the existing `/admin/config` Config tab (next to the S-notify-5b notification toggles + delivery-health panel). **NO migration** (the table + its `INSERT/SELECT/UPDATE` grants exist from `0067`; DELETE stays REVOKEd; head stays `0067`), **NO new permission key** (reuses `config.update`, catalog stays **102**), **audit reuses `CONFIG_UPDATED`** (object_type=config — no new `event_type`, no `ALTER TYPE`), **NO WORM touch** (the editor only edits config; N9/R53/R32 unchanged).

**BE.** A shared **pure** parser module `services/notifications/calendar_spec.py` (`parse_working_days` [moved verbatim from `escalation._parse_working_days`] · `parse_holiday` [keeps the resolver's `str()` coercion so an int entry like `20260101` still parses → resolver byte-identical] · `is_valid_timezone`) is imported by **both** the fail-safe `resolve_working_calendar` (refactored to it, the private fn deleted) **and** the fail-loud editor — so **validation parity can't drift, by construction (one code path, not two parallel assertions)**. A thin service `calendar_admin.py`: `get_working_calendar` (the `is_default` row `.limit(1)` as a view, **sanitized** through the parsers kept-good, OR a synthesized Mon-Fri default `{tz=organization.timezone, exists:false}` on the no-row edge) + `update_working_calendar` (validate fail-loud → **atomic `ON CONFLICT (org_id) WHERE is_default DO UPDATE`** upsert → audit-on-diff; **does NOT commit — the route commits**, the `api/config.py` precedent). `GET`/`PUT /admin/notifications/working-calendar` (both `Depends(config.update)`, org from `caller.org_id`) + openapi (2 paths + 2 schemas). The PUT body is **`list[Any]`** (NOT `list[int]`/`list[str]`).

**FE.** A self-contained `admin/WorkingCalendarEditor.tsx` in `ConfigAdmin` (between the toggles and the health panel; relies on the parent's GET-`/admin/config`-403 gate for no-access): a labelled Mantine **`Checkbox.Group`** week mask (string[]→`Number()`→sorted-unique ints; ≥1 enforced) · a native **`<input type=date>`** holiday list (blank-Add guard, deduped+sorted, distinct `Remove holiday {date}` labels) · an **editable** curated/searchable timezone `Select` (the `timezones.ts` idiom) · a **value-equality dirty-diff over canonical (sorted-unique) arrays** · a single Save (PUT). + 2 hooks (`useWorkingCalendar`/`useUpdateWorkingCalendar`, the unsaved-edit-clobber guards), 2 types, + MSW base GET/PUT handlers.

**Confirmed forks (AskUserQuestion).** (1) **Timezone EDITABLE here** — a REVERSAL of the spec's first-pass "slaved to org profile": the pre-code spec-validation proved the slaving premise FALSE — `set_org_profile` is reachable only from the `SetupWizard`, which `App.tsx` redirects away from once OPERATIONAL, so there is **no operational UI to change the org tz**; a read-only "change it on the org profile" note would point at a dead surface. So the editor owns the business-day tz operationally (it may diverge from the R8 effective-date tz — accepted). (2) native date input, **allow past**, deduped+sorted. (3) GET synthesizes a Mon-Fri default (`exists:false`) on the no-row edge, PUT upserts.

**Process: spec-first → a 6-lens adversarial spec-validation → a 6-task subagent-driven TDD build → a 3-lens whole-branch review → live-smoke → Codex.** ⚠ **The spec-validation (6 lenses → dedup → refute-first verify → triage) found 22 distinct findings, ALL confirmed real, and folded every one in BEFORE code** — it reversed the timezone premise (above) and **empirically pinned the central parity fix:** on this project's **pydantic 2.13.4 (lax mode)** a `working_days: list[int]` body **silently coerces** `[true]→[1]`, `["1"]→[1]`, `[1.0]→[1]` (HTTP 200) and 422s `[1.5]` **at Pydantic** → the strict bool/float/string guards would be **dead code** and the "rejects exactly what the resolver degrades" guarantee FALSE → declare the body **`list[Any]`** so every value reaches the strict service parser (one uniform service 422 mirroring the resolver's degrade). Other folded findings: **duplicate `working_days` are deduped + ACCEPTED** (NOT 422 — the resolver dedups; a 422 would itself break parity); **holiday parity is asymmetric** (the resolver SKIPS-kept-good a bad holiday, the editor REJECTS it → framed "editor ⊇ resolver", not bidirectional); the **atomic `ON CONFLICT` upsert** (a bare check-then-INSERT races the partial-unique `uq_working_calendar_one_default` → an unhandled IntegrityError/500); **value-equality dirty-diff** over canonical arrays (reference `!==` reads permanently-dirty after the post-save reseed — the S-notify-3b post-save-reset class); **MSW base handlers** for the 2 new endpoints (else `ConfigAdmin.test.tsx`'s success-path suites break under `onUnhandledRequest:"error"` once the editor mounts); input bounds (holidays ≤1000 / working_days ≤31); audit `CONFIG_UPDATED` **only on a real diff** (no no-op WORM rows); the **no-commit-service / route-commits** boundary (makes the INSERT-branch test leak-free — the app role can't DELETE a `working_calendar` row and the org FK is RESTRICT, so a *committed* calendar in a throwaway org can't be cleaned up — the S-notify-4 leaked-org trap). ⚠ **The 3-lens whole-branch review: diff-critic CLEAN · web-test-trap-reviewer CLEAN (both anti-tautology claims mutation-verified — removing the `onSuccess` invalidate and dropping `hasDay` each correctly broke a test) · opus whole-branch READY** (all 7 load-bearing invariants verified end-to-end). A per-task review caught one **Important** mid-build (the INSERT-branch could skip the audit if the first Save matched the synthesized defaults → `before_fields={}` when `not exists` so the audit always fires on first-create).

**Live-smoke (Chrome MCP, end-to-end).** Rebuilt web/api/worker/beat (no migration); demo (System Administrator) holds `config.update` natively (no override). Drove `/admin/config` → Working calendar: the editor loaded AHT's seed exactly (Mon-Fri, no holidays, America/Chicago, "Default", Save disabled) → added holiday `2026-07-03` (chip + distinct remove button + Save enabled) → Save → "Saved." + Save re-disabled (value-equality reset) + persisted → **a worker-container snippet proved the saved holiday SHIFTS a business-day threshold** (a reminder 1 business day before Mon 2026-07-06 lands Fri 07-03 WITHOUT the holiday, **Thu 07-02 WITH** it — the end-to-end SLA proof) + the `CONFIG_UPDATED` audit-on-diff (add+remove = 2 rows, no no-op pollution) → removed → AHT restored pristine.

⚠ **Codex — round 1, 3×P2 (all genuine, all fixed + thread-resolved; CI green; owner merged on approval).** (1) **calendar-tz durability** — the editor's tz was NOT durable: `set_org_profile` is API-reachable (latch-exempt `/api/v1/setup/*`) and *unconditionally* re-synced `working_calendar.timezone`, clobbering an operator-set tz → `set_org_profile` now syncs the default calendar **only where `timezone == <org's old tz>`** (preserve a customized tz; on first setup the seed calendar tz == org old tz so the S-notify-6 sync still applies). (2) **raw audit `before`** — the audit `before` used the *sanitized* `get_working_calendar` view, hiding a malformed/legacy stored value the upsert overwrites → now reads the **raw `is_default` row** (`_load_default`); a clean row's raw values already equal the canonical `after`, so no-op detection is unchanged. (3) **save synthesized calendar** — a calendar-less org (`exists:false`) couldn't Save the synthesized default (not dirty → Save disabled) → `canSave = (dirty || !cal.data.exists) && validName && hasDay`. Each fix has a covering test (the raw-`[5,1,3]`-survives audit test · the customized-tz-preserved setup test · `exists:false`→Save-enabled).

**Named residuals (not faked):** the **due_at-snap at materialize** (un-numbered) · the **claim-threshold-filter tautology** (`remind_2_sent_at IS NULL` always true) · the **distinct `remind_2`** · **escalate_2** · **`capa.overdue`** · **multiple named calendars per org** (this editor governs the single `is_default` row only) · **holiday recurrence / bulk import** (a flat date list) · a **2-session no-row INSERT race test** (structurally moot for the atomic `ON CONFLICT` — the plan downgraded it to optional). **Tests:** api unit **1032→1037** (+5: `test_calendar_spec` — valid/dedup-accept · the bool/float/string/empty/range rejections · `parse_holiday` str-coercion incl. the int-`20260101` byte-identical pin · `is_valid_timezone`; `test_working_calendar_resolve` repointed to the shared module, unchanged count); **+9 api integration** (`test_working_calendar_admin`: GET synth-vs-persisted-round-trip · INSERT-no-commit · validation-parity matrix [service-originated 422s + dup-accept] · UPDATE+audit-count + no-op-no-audit · 403 · the raw-audit-`before` test; + 1 setup customized-tz-preserved); web **1286→1292** (+6: `WorkingCalendarEditor` render/a11y · dirty round-trip reset · ≥1-weekday mutation-verify · holiday add/remove/blank-guard · the 2 `exists` Save-gate tests). (S-notify-7, BE+FE, NO migration [head stays `0067`], NO new key [catalog 102], api unit 1032→1037 +9 integration, web 1286→1292, PR #289 squash `03419ce`; Codex 1 round / 3 P2s all fixed.)

### S-notify-6 — business-day escalation SLAs: wire `working_calendar` into the timer sweep (R29 close-out; BE-only; migration `0067`; PR #287 squash `e08da6e`)

**What shipped — the second functional half of R29.** S-notify-4 shipped the durable `timer_sweep` Beat + the manager-graph escalation recipient resolution, but computed reminder/overdue/escalation thresholds with **raw wall-clock `timedelta`s** (a "3 days before due" reminder fired across the weekend; a "1 day after due" escalation pinged a manager on a Saturday). This slice adds the missing **`working_calendar`** entity and computes the **reminder (before-due) + escalation (after-due) OFFSETS** as **business days** against the org's calendar (skip weekends + holidays). **NO new permission key** (R38, catalog stays **102**), **NO web/openapi change** (BE-only), **NO WORM touch**.

**Migration `0067`:** a new operational `working_calendar` table — `id, org_id` (FK→organization RESTRICT), `name`, `working_days` jsonb (ISO weekday mask 1=Mon..7=Sun), `holidays` jsonb (`YYYY-MM-DD` list), **`timezone`** (IANA TEXT default `UTC` — additive to doc-14's column list, **owner fork D-2**: the calendar owns its own tz, seeded = `organization.timezone`), `is_default` bool, `created_at`/`updated_at` + a **partial unique index** `uq_working_calendar_one_default (org_id) WHERE is_default` (migration-managed in `env.py._MIGRATION_MANAGED_INDEXES`, absent from the ORM — the `ix_task_timer_pending` precedent) + **REVOKE DELETE** (keep INSERT/SELECT/UPDATE — operational config for the deferred editor, the notification-ledger posture, NOT `sla_policy`'s SELECT-only) + a **per-org seed** (one Mon-Fri `is_default` calendar, `timezone = organization.timezone`, raw `INSERT … CAST(:x AS JSONB)` + `json.dumps` for bulletproof serialization). `sla_policy` UNCHANGED — the stored Interval offsets are reinterpreted as business days (the S-notify-4 "slots in with no schema change" prediction held). **Downgrade** = `drop_index` then `drop_table` (no inbound FK → clean on a populated DB, no NOT-EXISTS guard).

**The math** (`services/notifications/timer.py`, kept pure/session-free): a frozen `Calendar(working_weekdays, holidays, tz)` value object + `is_working_day` · `shift_business_days(anchor, n, direction)` (walk day-by-day, count only working days, anchor NOT counted, bounded loop) · `business_threshold(due_at, offset, direction)` (UTC due_at → `cal.tz` local date → shift N working days → recombine local time-of-day → back to UTC; whole-day component walks business days, any sub-day remainder applied as wall-clock) · `DEFAULT_CALENDAR` (Mon-Fri/UTC). `due_steps` gains a `calendar` param: REMIND_1/2 use `BEFORE` (fire EARLIER than raw — skip the weekend backward, giving real working-day lead time), ESCALATE_1 uses `AFTER` (fire LATER — never over a weekend/holiday); **OVERDUE stays `now >= due_at`, unshifted (D-5).** The existing `due_steps` unit tests pass via an `ALL_DAYS` (7-day) calendar that degenerates to raw. **Wiring** (`escalation.py`): `resolve_working_calendar(session, org_id)` reads the org's `is_default` row → builds the pure `Calendar`, **fail-safe** (missing row / structurally-broken `working_days` / unknown `timezone` → `DEFAULT_CALENDAR`+warn; per-bad-holiday skip kept-good; a **non-list `holidays` scalar** → no holidays [the review fix]); resolved **once per locked per-task txn**, threaded into `due_steps`. The advisory-lock + FOR-UPDATE-SKIP-LOCKED + populate_existing + one-commit-per-task idempotency is UNCHANGED; `_due_task_ids` (stamp-null superset) is UNCHANGED.

**The OVERDUE decision (D-5, owner-ratified post-spec-validation).** ⚠ **A pre-code 5-lens/8-agent spec-validation (lens L1) proved the spec's original OVERDUE rationale FACTUALLY FALSE:** it claimed `due_at` is "already business-day-derived via a `due_in: N business_days` materialize path" — that path **does not exist**. `engine._due_at` is raw wall-clock (`now()+timedelta(hours=…)`; seeded `default_sla={'hours':120}` = 120 clock-hours), so `due_at` frequently lands on a weekend → an unshifted OVERDUE fires `task.overdue` (escalation-class, pierce-eligible) on weekends, which doc 10 §9.5 forbids. **Owner fork (AskUserQuestion):** keep OVERDUE raw at `due_at` (this slice shifts only the OFFSETS — overdue has no offset) + name the upstream **due_at-snap at materialize** as a still-deferred reconcile; *rejected* snapping OVERDUE in the timer (it would defeat the critical-overdue weekend pierce). ⚠ **The "R39" label was a stale mis-citation** — `engine._due_at`'s "deferred, R39" docstring (which the spec echoed) is wrong; the register's R39 is the Audits/CAPA decision. **The due_at-snap residual is UN-NUMBERED** (its own future register call); the engine docstring + register R29 as-built note + the spec §8 were corrected in this slice.

**Owner forks (AskUserQuestion ×2 + the D-5 fork):** BE-only (the `config.update`-gated admin editor deferred) · the `timezone` column on the calendar seeded from `organization.timezone` · keep OVERDUE raw.

**Process: spec-first → pre-code 5-lens spec-validation → 7-task TDD build → 3-lens convergence review → live-smoke.** ⚠ **The spec-validation (L2/L3/L4 design-sound; L1+L5 design-flawed, all confirmed, zero refuted) caught two MAJORS before code:** L1 (the false OVERDUE premise, above) + L5 (the test harness — "create-own-org + own SlaPolicy" is UNWORKABLE: the app role is SELECT-only on `sla_policy` so a fresh org has no policy + the `is_default` resolver + the per-org default-unique index + the DELETE-revoked `working_calendar` cleanup deadlock all conspire → rewrote to reuse-AHT's-seeded-policies + pre-stamp + build dates in the calendar's own tz + UPDATE-AHT-and-restore). ⚠ **The 3-lens convergence review:** diff-critic CLEAN · migration-reviewer CLEAN (independently round-tripped PG16 incl. the CI-blind seed path + verified grants/FK/index live) · worker-safety READY with **one Minor** (a non-list `holidays` JSONB scalar `5`/`true` raised an uncaught `TypeError` at `for h in row.holidays`, silently stalling that org's tasks forever — the broad sweep `except` swallows it cohort-wide but the org never fires; fixed `isinstance(list) else []`, symmetric with the `working_days` guard, + a regression test). ⚠ **THE test traps (build-discovered):** (1) once the timer applies the Mon-Fri calendar, the ~14 existing escalation integration tests using `datetime.now(UTC)` + `due_at = now-2d` became **weekday-flaky** (break when CI runs on a Sunday: `due_at`=Friday → business escalate threshold=Monday > Sunday `now`) → pin `now`/`_BASE` to a fixed **Wednesday**; (2) but `_BASE` was `2032` and `audit_event` is **monthly-partitioned by `occurred_at` with ONLY 2026-06/07/08 created at install** (migration 0010; the `roll_partitions` Beat doesn't run in tests) → the `TASK_ESCALATED` audit insert failed `"no partition of relation audit_event found"` → `_BASE` = `2026-06-24` (a Wednesday IN the 2026-06 partition) serves both the non-audit reminder/overdue tests AND the escalation tests. The anti-tautology weekend test was **mutation-verified** (FAILS against the old raw escalate math). ⚠ The PostToolUse **ruff `--fix` hook strips a just-added import** if no code uses it yet (F401) → add the using code first.

**Live-smoke (BE-driven, no UI):** rebuilt api/worker/beat/migrate, applied **0066→0067 on the POPULATED dev DB** (head `0067`); the seed produced `Default / [1,2,3,4,5] / [] / America/Chicago` (the dev org's **real, non-UTC** tz — proving per-org tz propagation on real data) `is_default=t`; grants exactly `INSERT,SELECT,UPDATE` (REVOKE DELETE live); a real `resolve_working_calendar` → Mon-Fri/America-Chicago + a real `timer_sweep()` → `{tasks:0, steps:0}` (the wired path runs clean on real data). The business-day BEHAVIOR (weekend escalation skip · resolver · fail-safe · idempotency · 2-session concurrency) is integration-test-proven against a real migrated PG16.

⚠ **Codex — 2 rounds, 6 findings (all genuine, none nitpicks, all fixed + thread-resolved; CI green each round).** **Round 1 (3×P2):** (1) **off-calendar firing** — a DELAYED sweep (worker down / template missing over a weekend) fired a reminder/escalation on a non-working day even though the threshold was a working day → `due_steps` now gates REMIND/ESCALATE on `is_working_day(now.astimezone(cal.tz).date())` (OVERDUE exempt, D-5) → defers the ping to the next working day; (2) **non-array `working_days`** — a JSON *string* `"67"` is iterable → wrongly became `{6,7}` → require `isinstance(list)`; (3) **setup tz sync** — the 0067 seed captured the org tz at MIGRATION time (UTC pre-setup), and `set_org_profile` updated only `Organization.timezone` → it now also UPDATEs the default `working_calendar.timezone` (a non-UTC org's SLAs were evaluating against UTC). **Round 2 (2×P2 + 1×P3) — all refinements of round-1's own fixes:** (4) **fallback dropped a valid tz** — round-1's `is_working_day(now)` gate *created* this: a `working_days` fallback to `DEFAULT_CALENDAR` (UTC) made the gate judge weekends in UTC for a non-UTC org → `resolve_working_calendar` restructured to resolve the **tz FIRST** and keep it through any weekdays fallback (only the weekdays → Mon-Fri); (5) **silent int coercion** — `int(x)` coerced floats/bools (`[1.9,2]`/`[true,2]`, since `bool` is an `int` subclass) → a new pure `_parse_working_days` requires a non-empty array of real ints 1..7 (no bool/float/string); (6) **`shift_business_days` exhaustion** (P3) — a sparse-workweek + >1yr-holiday calendar exhausted the bounded loop and returned an arbitrary (possibly non-working) date → could fire a timer EARLY → now returns a far-future sentinel `date(9999,1,1)` (NOT `date.max` — combining `date.max` with a westward-tz offset overflows `datetime` in `business_threshold`). Each fix has a test.

**Named residuals (not faked):** the **due_at-snap at materialize** (un-numbered — the upstream weekend-OVERDUE fix) · the **`config.update`-gated admin editor** (GET/PUT + Config-tab UI) · the **claim-threshold-filter tautology** (`remind_2_sent_at IS NULL` is always true → every open task re-claimed each sweep; 0-step no-op, bounded) · the **distinct second reminder** (`remind_2`) · **escalate_2** (reassign-from-pool / NEEDS_ATTENTION, doc 10 §9.5 E2) · **`capa.overdue`** · **multiple named calendars per org** (v1 uses `is_default` only) · **holiday recurrence / bulk import** (v1 is a flat date list) · the (v1-unused) **sub-day-remainder** offset behavior (pinned by a unit test; no production caller). **Tests:** api unit **1005→1032** (+27: the business-day helpers · `due_steps`-with-calendar · sub-day-remainder · the working-day-gate weekend+holiday gates · the shift exhaustion + westward-tz no-overflow · 9 `_parse_working_days` cases); **api integration** the resolver suite (reads-default / missing→DEFAULT / malformed-holidays / bad-working_days-keeps-tz / the anti-tautology weekend wiring test) + the setup org-profile calendar-tz-sync assertion; the ~14 existing escalation sweep tests hardened to the fixed Wednesday `_BASE`; web unchanged (**1286**). (S-notify-6, BE-only, migration **0067** [head `0066`→`0067`], api unit 1005→1032, web 1286, PR #287 squash `e08da6e`; Codex 2 rounds / 6 findings all fixed.)

### S-notify-5c — SSE for the notification bell (slice 5c, the LAST Notification-family slice; BE+FE+1 Caddy line; NO migration [head stays `0066`]; PR #285 squash `7505e58`)
