- **S-context-2** (read consumer — the FIRST consumer of the Context register's GOVERNING snapshot; BE-only, mirrors S-risk-4a) — **`GET /context/summary` projects the clause-4.1 register's GOVERNING (current Effective) frozen `{rows}` snapshot via the new pure `domain/context/summary.summarize_register` → `{published, total, by_classification, by_category, by_status, active, never_reviewed}` — the CONTROLLED read-of-record (never the live working satellite), for a future Home/dashboard tile + the Context SPA (S-context-fe).** **What shipped (NO migration [head stays `0060`], NO new permission key [rides the seeded `register.read`, catalog 102]; contract = the `/context/summary` path + a `ContextRegisterSummary` schema):** (1) **`domain/context/summary.py`** — a pure, I/O-free projection (the `domain/risk/summary` sibling, but clause 4.1 has NO graded axis → NO `criteria`/`resolve_criteria`, strictly categorical counts): `by_classification` (internal/external — the ISO spine), `by_category` (the SWOT axis + an `uncategorized` bucket for NULL category), `by_status` (active/closed), `active` headline (= `by_status.active`, the `high_risk` analogue), `never_reviewed` (rows with no `last_reviewed_at` — a CLOCK-FREE freshness signal; a time-based "stale" would need a policy threshold + `now`, deferred); defensive `if x in bucket` guards (an unknown enum value falls out of the breakdown but still counts in `total` — the risk posture); every leaf a JSON `int` (survives `rfc8785.dumps` if a consumer freezes it). (D-3) **one slice** (collapses to the endpoint + the shared seam once the MR consumer is deferred). **⚠ Traps a future session MUST carry:** (1) the summary is the GOVERNING read-of-record (the S-risk-2/-4a posture) — an UnderRevision steward edit is invisible until the next publish/release; the integration `summ2 == summ` byte-equality after a live ADD during UnderRevision is the read-of-record proof (the new row appears in `GET /context` but NOT in the governing summary); (2) `/context/summary` must mount before `/context/{issue_id}` — and a no-grant **403 test alone can't catch a shadow** (the `{issue_id}` route would ALSO 403), so the guard is a route-RESOLUTION unit test asserting the endpoint NAME; load-bearing, not decorative — the S-risk-4a precedent); (5) **a ruff-VERSION drift between the local pre-commit `ruff-format` (pinned `v0.6.9`) and CI's uv-ruff (`0.15.17`) wraps a multi-line `assert cond, (msg)` DIFFERENTLY** — only a long endpoint name like `context_summary_endpoint` pushed the inline form over 100 cols and triggered the split → the two fight (pre-commit reformats → commit aborts; uv re-reformats → CI). The fix is a CROSS-VERSION-STABLE single-line form (`expected = "…"; assert name == expected, f"… {expected}"`), NOT `--no-verify` (the #241 "hooks match CI" claim still has a ruff-format rev gap). **Named residuals (not faked):** **MR 9.3.2(b)** context-change input → **S-interested-parties-1** (both the 4.1 context + 4.2 interested-parties halves together); **S-context-fe** = the Context SPA (register page / SWOT view / the summary tile reading `GET /context/summary` / `RegisterLifecyclePanel`); the carried-over server-computed `can_release`/`can_manage` on `GET /risks/register` (+ `/context/register`) — rides S-context-fe. **Test delta: +7 api unit** (`test_context_summary.py` — empty→zeros, classification/category [+`uncategorized` for NULL]/status counts, the `active` headline, `never_reviewed`, defensive unknown-enum; `test_context_routes.py` — `/context/summary` resolves to `context_summary_endpoint` not the `{issue_id}` shadow) **+3 api integration** (`test_context_summary_endpoint.py`: the strong positive + **read-of-record invariance** [publish→release an internal issue → `published:true` + governing counts; then start-revision + ADD a live issue → the summary is BYTE-IDENTICAL while `GET /context` shows the new row]; the no-grant **403**; the deterministic `published == has_governing` invariant); **web unchanged.** api unit 896→903. ruff/format/mypy-strict clean (Kubuntu clean local gate); redocly clean; CI green (all 4 integration shards + api/web/migrations/contracts/security). **diff-critic CLEAN; a 3-lens adversarial Workflow (read-of-record · authz/403-vs-filter · test-determinism) returned 0 confirmed defects.** **Merge gate:** green CI + both in-house reviews clean + owner's explicit "squash merge". - **S-context-1** (backend core **+ lifecycle together** — model + migration + content + service + lifecycle + `/context` routes + openapi + tests; the owner-forked scope, vs the risk family's 1→1b split) — **a true controlled Context register: org-level `context_issue` rows are version CONTENT of a `kind=DOCUMENT` singleton `CTX` head, FSM-revision-edited then frozen at publish; CRUD + the full publish/freeze/release lifecycle ship in one slice.** **What shipped (migration `0060`, NO new permission key — rides the already-seeded `register.read`/`register.manage`; catalog stays 102; NO role grant [org-level — see below]; contract = the `/context` endpoints + 5 schemas):** (1) **`context_issue`** = a 1:many satellite of the `CTX` head (own `id` PK + `register_doc_id` FK + `row_version`; the R49 register-row shape, NOT a shared-PK subtype) carrying the **enriched** model (the owner fork): `classification` enum(`internal`,`external`) [the ISO clause-4.1 spine, NOT NULL] + `category` enum(`strength`,`weakness`,`opportunity`,`threat`) [the optional **SWOT** axis, NULLABLE] + `status` enum(`active`,`closed`) [a new issue is always `active`; retire by closing, never delete] + `description` + `last_reviewed_at`; **NO `process_id`** (org-level). (2) **Pure `domain/context/register_content.py`** — `build_register({rows})` (rows-only, **NO `criteria` block** — clause 4.1 has no computed/graded axis, so **no `resolve_criteria`, no derive-and-freeze**, strictly simpler than risk) + `register_needs_freeze`. (4) **`api/context.py`** — `/context` CRUD + `/context/register{,/start-revision,/publish,/release}`, gated by scope — the ROW surface + the steward acts are @ **SYSTEM** (`GET /context` filter-not-403 [a no-grant caller → 200 + empty; all-or-nothing at the org scope], `GET /context/{id}` enforces `register.read` @ SYSTEM, POST/PATCH + start-revision/publish `register.manage` @ SYSTEM; no body/path scope, no PATCH-reassign re-auth) — **but** `GET /context/register` (the head lifecycle status) is readable by **any authenticated org member** (`Depends(get_current_user)`, org-level, not row-sensitive), and **release enforces `document.release` over the MULTI-AXIS `_register_release_scope`** (artifact_id + folder_path + document_level + lifecycle_state + SoD-2), **NOT `ResourceContext.system()`** — the S-risk-5 release posture, so a future S-context-fe / `can_release` must NOT use a single-axis SYSTEM `/me/permissions` probe (it would hide release from a caller whose scoped `document.release` grant the server WOULD accept; the named `can_release` residual is the faithful gate); static `/context/register*` BEFORE `/context/{issue_id}` (S-pack-2 shadow guard, route-resolution unit-tested). (5) **Reservation GENERALIZED** — `reject_rsk_register_mutation` → `reject_managed_register_mutation` keyed by `_MANAGED_REGISTERS = {RSK, CTX}` (per-code message; RSK byte-identical), reserving the CTX head from every generic document mutation + the ingestion-import guard, exactly as RSK. **4 owner decisions (AskUserQuestion ×2):** enriched content model (SWOT + status + last_reviewed beyond the minimal contract); ride `register.*` (catalog 102); **4.2 Interested Parties = a SEPARATE register** (own head/table/slice, per the two-table contract); **core+lifecycle together** in one slice. **⚠ Codex was THE authz edge-finder over 2 rounds (2 real findings) a CLEAN migration-reviewer + diff-critic + a 3-lens adversarial Workflow [0 confirmed] ALL missed — the recurring "Codex finds the authz edge past clean in-house reviews" pattern:** **P1** — generalizing the *mutation* guard to `{RSK, CTX}` left the generic `POST /documents` **create** path's SEPARATE inline `dt.code == "RSK"`-only check unguarded → once 0060 seeds the CTX type, a `document.create` holder could mint an arbitrary CTX doc (with ProcessLinks) that `context.find_head` (oldest non-Obsolete CTX head) would adopt — invariant break + escalation → added **`reject_managed_register_creation(code)`** keyed by the same map, wired into the create endpoint (RSK response byte-identical). **P2** — the CREATE-DCR **implement** path (`_resolve_implement_version`) guarded OBJ/MR shared-PK subtypes but NOT the register heads: a freshly-published register (Approved, `current_effective_version_id` still null) could be supplied as a CREATE DCR's `resulting_version_id` and released via the GENERIC cutover, bypassing `/risks|/context/register/release`'s document.release+SoD-2 → **this was a pre-existing RSK gap S-risk-1b's `_resolve_target` reservation missed**; ## RISK & OPPORTUNITY REGISTER — clause 6.1 Risks & Opportunities (the FIRST register family; R18/R49; migration 0058–0059)

- **S-risk-5** (the in-app register-steward lifecycle console — closes the F-1 deferral S-risk-4b named; **with it the clause-6.1 family is not just complete end-to-end but FULLY SELF-SERVICE in-app** — the steward no longer needs the API / a SYSTEM override to run the register's controlled-document cycle) — **a "Register lifecycle" card on `RisksRegisterPage` that drives the THREE steward-only acts (start-revision → publish → release); the approve/decide step keeps riding the existing `/tasks` DOCUMENT arm (an RSK version is a `subject_type=DOCUMENT` task → `ReviewApprovePage`'s generic redline + `DecisionCard`) with ZERO new FE.** **What shipped (FE-only, NO migration [head stays `0059`], NO new permission key [rides `register.manage` / `document.release`, catalog 102], NO contract change — the 3 lifecycle endpoints already shipped in S-risk-1b + were documented in `openapi.yaml`):** (1) **`RegisterLifecyclePanel`** — a bordered card rendered only for a steward (`canManage || canRelease`, quiet absence for everyone else), gating each button on STATE × permission (the RSK head has NO server `capabilities` block, unlike OBJ): **Publish** on Draft/UnderRevision, **Start revision** on Effective, **Release** on Approved, an "in review — an approver decides in Tasks" note (+ a `/tasks` link) on InReview. (4) **`RisksRegisterPage`** renders the panel; the read-only banner stays informational for non-stewards (the console, not the shared banner, carries the CTA — preserving the S-risk-4b "don't instruct what a viewer can't do" rule). **Gating asymmetry (load-bearing):** start-revision/publish probe **`register.manage` @ SYSTEM** (the backend `_register_manage_system` FORCES SYSTEM — a bound Process-Owner can't steward the org head); (b) gating Publish on the client `rows.length` wrongly disabled it for a `register.manage`-without-`register.read` steward (`GET /risks` is register.read-filtered → 0 rows for a non-empty register) → **drop the client row-count gate; the **FE `/me/permissions` probe is single-axis by API design (`resource_for_scope` populates exactly ONE axis)**, so NO FE probe can; the only faithful fix is a SERVER-COMPUTED capability → **owner chose DEFER (v1 `document.release` is SYSTEM-override-only, so the gap is non-v1 + fail-safe — a hidden button, the server-403 stays the boundary), thread resolved declined-with-rationale.** **⚠ Traps a future session MUST carry:** (1) a steward console that mirrors an enforce by probing only ONE scope is correct ONLY when the backend FORCES that scope (register.manage @ SYSTEM is) — when the backend builds a multi-axis doc-resource scope (document.release does), a single-axis FE probe is structurally incomplete; (2) NEVER gate an affordance on a `register.read`-FILTERED count (a manage-without-read actor sees 0 for a non-empty register) — let the server's 409 decide; (3) the faithful gate for a multi-axis backend scope is a SERVER-COMPUTED capability boolean (the OBJ `capabilities` / S-leadership CX-1 pattern), not an FE permission probe. **Named residual (not faked): a server-computed `can_release` (+ `can_manage` for symmetry) capability on `GET /risks/register`** — reusing `_register_release_scope` verbatim — the proper closure of the Codex r2 multi-axis gap (a v1.x BE follow-up; - **S-risk-4b** (the Risk & Opportunity register SPA — the LAST slice; **with it the clause-6.1 family is COMPLETE end-to-end**) — **the web surface the register has lacked: a register page + a hand-rolled 5×5-matrix SVG + a detail drawer with the risk→CAPA spawn seam + a Home PLAN high-risk line + the `/risks` route, all row-surface-only per the ratified F-1 (the register-steward lifecycle UI stays deferred).** **What shipped (FE-only, NO migration [head stays `0059`], NO new permission key [rides `register.read`/`register.manage`/`capa.create`, catalog 102]; the drawer's `sys.can ‖ proc.can` would show actions for a row in a process-DENY carved out of a SYSTEM grant → **for a process-owned row use the effective PROCESS probe ALONE** (it folds matching SYSTEM grants + scoped DENYs; reopening rides the API / a SYSTEM override in v1); the `?risk=` sync effect didn't follow the param's REMOVAL (back/forward left the drawer open) → **key the effect on the risk param alone + sync to null** (a filter-param change must not close a local open — +a regression test). **DECLINED (both rounds, same rationale): "probe ALL readable processes, not just the first"** — the ratified S-capa-raise-process O(1) first-readable-process trade-off; - **S-risk-1b** (the controlled-document publish/freeze/release lifecycle — closes the named S-risk-1 deferral) — **the RSK register head becomes a true controlled Effective document: risk rows are version CONTENT, edited through FSM revisions, FROZEN (rows + per-method scoring criteria) into immutable versions at publish; the live band grades against the GOVERNING version's frozen criteria, never live code (R49 L2; the objectives derive-and-freeze precedent verbatim).** **What shipped (NO migration [head stays `0058`], NO new permission key [catalog 102]; contract = 4 new `/risks/register/*` endpoints + `RiskRegisterStatus`/`RiskRegisterPublish` schemas):** (1) **Pure `domain/risk/register_content.py`** — `build_register({rows,criteria})` / `criteria_for_methods` / `resolve_criteria(governing, scoring_method)` / `register_needs_freeze` (mirrors `domain/objectives/commitment.py`; rows sorted by id for a reproducible WORM body; criteria a per-method map keyed by `scoring_method.value`). (3) **`services/risk/lifecycle.py`** — `start_register_revision` (T7 wrapper over the vault `start_revision`) + `publish_register` (the `submit_objective_for_review` shape: head FOR-UPDATE+populate_existing → `register_needs_freeze` → `checkin_risk_register` → drop the start-revision WorkingDraft [O-4] → `submit_review` → `instantiate_approval` → audit → commit → release the edit lock); `queries.governing_register` resolves the head's Effective version's frozen `risk_register` (PRIOR Effective while UnderRevision — R43). (4) **`api/risk.py`** — `POST /risks/register/{start-revision,publish,release}` + `GET /risks/register` status; the `_risk` serializer grades the band via `resolve_criteria(governing, …)`; the static `/risks/register*` routes mount BEFORE `/risks/{risk_id}` (S-pack-2). **Two owner decisions (AskUserQuestion):** (D-2b) **`register.manage` @ SYSTEM gates start-revision/publish** — the QMS Owner (holds it @ SYSTEM) stewards the register, a bound Process-Owner's PROCESS grant can't publish the org head; release on **`document.release` @ SYSTEM + SoD-2** (the OBJ release posture; SYSTEM override in v1). The OBJ surface-key precedent over the spec §2's loose "document.* SYSTEM override". (D-3b) **fold the managed-doc reservation in.** **Investigated, no config needed:** `instantiate_approval` is keyed by `WorkflowSubjectType.DOCUMENT` (the `document_approval` def) — **doc-type-agnostic** → RSK rides the SAME lightweight Approver/QMS-Owner stage OBJ/MR ride; an empty pool → `NEEDS_ATTENTION`. **The D-3b reservation, completed under Codex pressure — the RSK head is now reserved from EVERY content/lifecycle mutation:** generic metadata-PATCH / distribution / document-link (both branches + the link **target** + delete other-end), clause-mapping map/unmap (RSK-only), obsoletion at the **`lifecycle.obsolete` CHOKEPOINT** (covers the generic `/obsolete` route AND a RETIRE DCR that calls `obsolete()` directly), and **DCR targeting** at `_resolve_target` (RSK-only — closes a REVISE-DCR adopting the publish-Approved version + releasing it past the `/risks/register/release` SoD-2). The generic `/documents/{id}/release` is intentionally left open (authz-equivalent: same `document.release`+SoD-2+cutover, not a bypass). **⚠ THE structural lesson — the RSK head is a per-org SINGLETON shared across the one-org integration DB**, so a lifecycle test that drives it to Effective would 409 every OTHER test's risk-create (and break `test_risk_process_scope`); there is NO runtime multi-org bootstrap → the head-advancing test NORMALIZES the shared head to editable at the start + a **`restore_register_head` teardown fixture** returns it to UnderRevision even if the body fails mid-lifecycle (a `MissingGreenlet`-500 after `release()` had already committed the head Effective was the cascade CI shard-4 caught). **⚠ Codex was THE edge-finder again over 3 rounds a CLEAN diff-critic ×2 + green CI MISSED — 6 genuine fixes; the re-posts are STALE duplicates (the fixes present + CI-proven by the held-lock/reservation tests) → trim-don't-chase + ask the owner, don't loop:** round-1 (1 P1 + 3 P2): **the P1 version-integrity TOCTOU** — a concurrent `POST/PATCH /risks` row write could land AFTER publish freezes the version (row writers didn't hold publish's head lock), leaving live rows out of the SIGNED version → `add_risk_row`/`update_risk_row` now lock the head **FOR UPDATE** (consistent row→head order; publish locks only the head → deadlock-free; the S-records-W discipline), proven by a 2-session held-lock-blocks test; + the link-target / clause-mapping reservations. round-2 (1 new): the RETIRE-DCR obsolete bypass → the chokepoint. round-3 (1 new): **the empty-register publish race** — the first `POST /risks` commits the 0-row head in `resolve_or_create_head` BEFORE taking the head FOR UPDATE to insert, so a publish that locks the head in that window freezes an EMPTY version + 409s (loses) the first risk → `publish_register` rejects a zero-row register under the lock (closes the race + a sensible business rule). Plus the **release endpoint `MissingGreenlet`** (read status off `release()`'s `_cutover`-refreshed doc, NOT `expire_all`+re-read — the sync `_register_status` lazy-loaded otherwise). **⚠ Traps a future session MUST carry:** (1) the per-org-singleton head makes lifecycle tests pollute siblings → normalize-at-start + restore-on-teardown; (2) row writes must lock the head FOR UPDATE to serialize against the publish freeze (the version must contain EXACTLY the signed rows); (3) reserve the managed head at the SERVICE chokepoint when a path can reach it both via an endpoint AND a DCR (`lifecycle.obsolete`); (4) read post-release status off `release()`'s returned doc, never `expire_all`+re-read (sync-serializer `MissingGreenlet`); (5) **ruff strips just-added imports → body-first** (hit repeatedly: the api/risk + dcr/service + test imports + `contextlib`); (6) Codex re-posts fixed findings as stale duplicates anchored to the same hunk — verify the fix is present + CI-proven, resolve the thread, don't re-fix. **Named residuals (not faked):** the **FE** (`S-risk-4`); **S-risk-2** (read consumers + MR input-(e)) / **S-risk-3** (CAPA spawn); the no-freeze re-publish dedup branch (`register_needs_freeze` False) reasoned-correct but not directly asserted (diff-critic low-pri); OBJ/MR-as-DCR-target (pre-existing, out of scope); a register-steward role/UI for the org-head lifecycle. **Test delta: +14 api unit** (`test_risk_register_content.py` — build/criteria/resolve/needs-freeze + **the L2 proof** [a frozen criteria beats a live-code band re-grade] + the static-route-precedence resolution + RSK ∉ `LEADERSHIP_DOC_TYPES`) **+4 api integration test fns** (`test_risk_lifecycle.py`: the full publish→approve→release→Effective lifecycle + read-only-when-Effective + the frozen snapshot + revision/supersede + governing band + a **SoD-2 negative** [author self-release 403 `sod_violation`]; the head-steward 403 [PROCESS owner]; the reservation 422s [metadata/distribution/links/clause-mapping/obsolete/DCR-target + OBJ]; the held-lock race); **web unchanged.** ruff/format/mypy-strict clean (modulo the Windows `O_NOFOLLOW` baseline); redocly clean; CI 11/11 green (all 4 shards). **diff-critic CLEAN ×2 (original + final full-diff); Codex 3 rounds (6 fixed, all threads addressed/resolved).** **Merge gate:** green CI + Codex threads resolved + owner's explicit go. PR [#227](https://github.com/CoJoA13/EasySynQ/pull/227), squash `6b2fbd6`.

- **S-risk-1** (backend register core — model + migration + rules + service + `/risks` routes + openapi + tests) — **a working risk register: authorized users author/score/treat/read process-scoped risk rows with every load-bearing authz/re-derive invariant the spec's 5-lens panel surfaced.** **What shipped (migration `0058`, NO new permission key — rides the already-seeded `register.read`/`register.manage` [`0004:97-98`]; catalog stays 102; contract = the `/risks` endpoints + 6 schemas):** (1) **`risk_opportunity`** = a **1:many satellite** of a `kind=DOCUMENT` `RSK` head (own `id` PK + `register_doc_id` FK + `row_version`; NOT a shared-PK subtype like `quality_objective` — a register has many rows; the sibling `context_issue`/`interested_party` shape) carrying `type`/`description`/`process_id`/`clause_id`/`likelihood`/`severity`/`risk_rating`/`scoring_method`/`treatment`/`effectiveness`/`linked_capa_id` + the `likelihood`/`severity` BETWEEN-1-AND-5 CHECKs (bare-token names); the `risk_opportunity_type`+`scoring_method` enums + the additive `RISK_RESCORED` event type; the `RSK` document_type seed (`is_singleton`, all orgs); and **the `register.manage`→Process-Owner role grant with the `_PROCESS_SCOPE` template** (NOT `_SYSTEM_SCOPE` — the panel L1-CRITICAL: a SYSTEM template is exempt from `bound_scope` clamping → would match every process; an R38-additive grant, no new key). (2) **Pure `domain/risk/rules.py`** — `risk_rating = likelihood × severity` (1..25) + `risk_band` (total, criteria-PARAMETERIZED) + a 4-band RAG (Critical/High/Medium/Low + unscored) reusing the objectives tone/glyph vocabulary, with a **golden test** pinning each `scoring_method`'s criteria byte-shape (the L2 immutability guard). (3) **`services/risk/service.py`** — `resolve_or_create_head` (an advisory-lock-serialized get-or-create of the single non-Obsolete RSK head; the head carries **ZERO ProcessLinks** via `create_document(processes=())` — L1-MAJOR); `add_risk_row`/`update_risk_row` re-derive `risk_rating` on EVERY write (never client-supplied), gate edits to the head being Draft/UnderRevision, validate the clause against the org framework BEFORE head-create (no orphan), and **re-authorize `register.manage` over the row's CURRENT freshly-locked `process_id` after the `FOR UPDATE`** (the under-lock TOCTOU close); a re-score emits `RISK_RESCORED`. (4) **`/risks` routes** — filter-not-403 LIST (per-row `register.read`, NO `artifact_id` to avoid a shared-head leak, `source_ip` threaded), scoped GET, body-scope POST, a PATCH that gates on `process_id` **PRESENCE** (a `null` clear enforces at SYSTEM) and re-enforces the NEW target on reassign; `extra="forbid"` bodies. the import commit rejects `type_code "RSK"`. **⚠ Scope: the controlled-document publish/freeze/approval/release/revision lifecycle (+ the governing-snapshot band resolve) is DEFERRED to S-risk-1b (named)** — the head stays Draft (a working register), the golden test the L2 protection without versioning; the spec's "partial-unique single-head index" reconciled to a **service-level advisory-lock guard** (an RSK-specific partial-unique isn't expressible without breaking POL's draft-successor flow that the Effective-only `uq_doc_info_singleton_effective` deliberately allows). **⚠ Codex was THE authz edge-finder over 3 rounds a CLEAN diff-critic + migration-reviewer MISSED — 8 real findings fixed + 3 trimmed:** round-1 (2 P1 + 2 P2): the `{process_id:null}` clear bypassed re-auth (present-but-None → gate on PRESENCE); the generic `POST /documents` could mint a process-linked/second RSK head `_find_head` adopts (reserve RSK); clause-validated-after-head-create orphaned a doc; the under-lock TOCTOU. round-2 (1 P1 + 3 P2, all "the head reachable via another generic path"): the process-link-add + byte-path + import vectors → the shared `reject_rsk_register_mutation`. round-3 (3 P2, same class): the metadata/clause-mapping/distribution/document-link endpoints → **TRIMMED as a named residual** (privileged-actor SYSTEM/ARTIFACT `document.*` edges, NOT bound-owner escalations [the escalation — a ProcessLink on the head — IS closed]; at parity with the OBJ/MR managed-doc reservation which also guards only the byte path; comprehensively reserving the managed-doc family from EVERY generic endpoint is a cross-cutting follow-up — **trim-don't-chase**). **⚠ Traps a future session MUST carry:** (1) **a SYSTEM `scope_template` is exempt from `bound_scope` clamping** (`repository._grant_from_role`) → a PROCESS-scoped ROW grant MUST use `_PROCESS_SCOPE`, never the `clauseMap.read`/`_SYSTEM_SCOPE` precedent (an org-level resource = the OPPOSITE case). ## v1.x INCLUDE_SUBPROCESSES RECONCILE — PROCESS-grant descendant inclusion is v1.x-deferred (R48); the whole process-scope authz arc is now COMPLETE (docs-only, no migration, head stays 0057)

- **S-include-subprocesses** (reconcile `include_subprocesses` to v1 own-id-only + a binding R48 entry) — **the LAST named gap in the process-scope authz arc** (S-owner-assignment-1 [#209] → `GET /processes` row-filter [#213] → records R/W/C [#216/#217/#218] → CAPA-raise [#220] → **here**). docs/07 §5.1/§5.3/§9.1 + docs/15 §9.2 promised a `PROCESS` grant "optionally includes descendants (`include_subprocesses` flag, default true)", but the v1 PDP (`domain/authz/pdp.py` `_matches_scope`, PROCESS branch) matches PURELY on own-id intersection (`bool(scoped & resource.process_ids)`) and NEVER walks `process.parent_id` — the flag is unimplemented anywhere; owner-assignment mints an EXPLICIT `process_ids` set, and `_document_scope`/the records resolver/search/the `GET /processes`/`/map` row-filter all match on own-id/own-link sets. **SPEC-FIRST (a binding authz-model fork → owner's call, not a silent pick):** a 4-agent analysis Workflow (impl-surface map / adversarial 4-lens refute panel / doc-reconcile sweep / cost-alternatives) weighed IMPLEMENT vs RECONCILE; the refute panel returned `reopens_nonconverging_surface` (CRITICAL/unsafe) and the owner chose **RECONCILE-defer**. **What shipped (DOCS-ONLY, NO migration [head stays `0057`], NO new key, NO behavior change):** marked descendant inclusion **v1.x-deferred (v1 = own-id-only)** at the 4 forward-promise locations (07 §5.1 table PROCESS-row selector cell, §5.3 Processes inheritance bullet, §9.1 Diego persona bound-scope cell, 15 §9.2 scope-inheritance bullet) + a new **R48** decisions-register entry + bumped the register's OWN self-range `R1–R47 → R1–R48` (the intro line + the Part-3 heading). The factual `process.parent_id` self-FK schema (docs/14, the ERD `parent/subprocess` edge) is **UNCHANGED** — a process CAN nest; only its authz-grant inheritance is deferred. **⚠ WHY defer, not implement (the refute panel's CRITICAL finding):** expanding a PROCESS grant's `process_ids` to descendants at the SINGLE `gather_grants` grant-resolution chokepoint would **silently DEFEAT every per-target write re-auth guard** (`_enforce_target_process_record`, `_enforce_target_process`, the per-process `capa.create` gate) — each re-enforces against a single LITERAL target process id that the expanded grant would now intersect, re-opening exactly the non-converging records/CAPA **write-escalation** surface S-records-W deliberately trimmed to broad-only; a faithful `default true` flip would ALSO silently widen every existing bound Process-Owner grant at once (no grant carries the flag today). **⚠ The better future design (if v1.x ever implements it):** a materialized **ltree ancestry column** on `process` (mirror how FOLDER achieves ZERO-walk subtree inheritance via the `folder_path` string, R6 / `pdp.py` FOLDER branch) — its own slice (migration + backfill + reparent-rewrite + a resource-side path on EVERY `ResourceContext` builder) + its own register decision, **NOT** an on-the-fly grant-side expansion. **Verification:** the reconcile matches the proven code — the existing `test_process_owner_list_hides_unreadable_parent_id` (`tests/integration/test_process_scope.py`) already encodes own-id-only behavior (a bound child-owner does NOT reach a resource via the parent); diff-critic CLEAN (verified PDP own-id-only, all surfaces own-id/own-link, the cited test, R48 numbering/format/truthful no-migration claim, the 4-location consistency, markdown intact). **⚠ Codex P3 (the one finding): an R48 add leaves the register's own self-range labels stale at `R1–R47`** (intro + Part-3 heading) → bumped both. **⚠ A push/merge RACE dropped the P3 range-fix commit from the squash** — I pushed the fix (`7d3f401`) while the owner squash-merged the LAGGING PR head (`6e520db`); GitHub squashed the *displayed* head, so the range bump landed on the branch ref but NOT in the merged squash → **re-applied via this finish-slice follow-up** (the lesson: after a late push, VERIFY the PR head SHA before relying on a merge — a squash captures the registered head, not necessarily the branch tip). **Named residuals (NOT regressions; carried from the arc, none re-opened):** the v1.x descendant-inclusion itself (now bound as R48 + the ltree-ancestry future design); `init-upload` PROCESS-staging (S-records-W); Process-Owner CAPA/finding/document-evidence trimmed broad-only (S-records-W); the 2 round-6 correction-vs-link TOCTOUs (S-records-W); the CAPA-raise multi-role first-process-probe false-negative (S-capa-raise-process). **No test delta (docs-only; web/api counts unchanged).** PR [#222](https://github.com/CoJoA13/EasySynQ/pull/222) squash `8ba40a8` (the reconcile) + this finish-slice docs follow-up (re-applies the lost `R1–R48` range bump + the slice narrative).

## v1.x CAPA-RAISE PROCESS-SCOPE — a bound Process-Owner reaches + raises a CAPA from the board (closes the named owner-assignment CAPA-raise deferral; no migration, head stays 0057)

- **S-capa-raise-process** (wire the PROCESS-scoped CAPA raise from the board + scope the board's reads per-process) — **closes the long-deferred CAPA-Raise process-scope gap (Codex P1 on #102, named "UNBLOCKED but unwired" by S-owner-assignment-1), now exercisable because the owner-assignment binding [#209] mints a real PROCESS-scoped `capa.create` and the `GET /processes` row-filter [#213] populates the picker source.** **Scope GREW from FE-only → BE+FE mid-review** (owner-approved) when Codex showed the FE alone couldn't reach its target persona. **What shipped (BE+FE, NO migration [head stays `0057`], NO new permission key — rides `capa.create`/`capa.read`, catalog stays 102; contract = description text only):** **(FE)** (1) **`RaiseCapaModal`** gained an optional Process picker (`useProcesses()` from `objectives/hooks`, the `RaiseInitiativeModal` idiom; conditionally rendered when ≥1 process is readable) that submits `process_id` in the `CapaRaiseBody` — a process-less raise stays byte-identical to the SYSTEM/ad-hoc CAPA; (2) a `requireProcess` prop makes the picker **required** (label "Process" + placeholder "Pick the owning process"; submit gated on a pick) for a PROCESS-only creator, since a process-less raise authorizes at SYSTEM → 403; (3) the modal is now **conditionally mounted** (`{raiseOpen && <RaiseCapaModal …/>}`, the `RaiseInitiativeModal` precedent) so close unmounts + discards the draft (a picked-then-cancelled process can't bleed into the next raise); (4) **`CapaBoardPage`** Raise button shows when the caller holds `capa.create` at **SYSTEM OR their first readable process** (`usePermissions()` SYSTEM probe `||` a `usePermissions({level:"PROCESS",id:firstProcessId})` probe; `usePermissions(undefined)` dedupes to the SYSTEM query when there are no readable processes), and passes `requireProcess={!systemCanCreate}`. **(BE — the Codex P1 fix)** the board's own reads were SYSTEM-gated, so a *pure* bound Process-Owner 403'd `GET /capas` (`useCapas().forbidden` → the no-access panel) and never saw the button → applied the **S-process-scope-2 read-filter pattern** (a safe DECOUPLED read — a CAPA's `process_id` is set by an already-re-authorized `POST /capas`): (5) `GET /capas` moved from `require("capa.read")` (SYSTEM enforce) to `get_current_user` + a new **`_readable_capas`** per-row filter (`gather_grants("capa.read")` once → keep rows where `authorize(grants, "capa.read", _process_scope(row[0].process_id), ctx).allow`; **filter-not-403**, SYSTEM grants match every row byte-identical, `source_ip` threaded; a process-less ad-hoc CAPA needs a SYSTEM grant); (6) `GET /capas/{id}` + `/approval` moved to **`_capa_read_scoped = require("capa.read", async_scope_resolver=_capa_scope)`** (PROCESS-enforce; a SYSTEM Top-Management approver still matches; a bound owner reads their own process's CAPA; else 403). **Load-bearing decisions:** (a) **the button gate keys on `capa.create`, NEVER on "has readable processes"** — an Internal Auditor holds SYSTEM `process.read` (a non-empty process list) + SYSTEM `capa.read` (board access) but no `capa.create` at any scope, so gating on process-count would leak the button to auditors (and regress today's behaviour); the per-process `capa.create` probe is the only correct discriminator. (b) **The button gate is O(1)** — the owner chose `SYSTEM ‖ first-readable-process probe` over a `useQueries` fan-out across ALL readable processes, specifically to avoid firing N `/me/permissions` calls for every broad-`process.read` caller (an auditor → all org processes) on each board load; the owner-assignment binding mints `process.read` + `capa.create` over the SAME bound set, so for a single-role bound owner every readable process is a createable one (first is representative). (c) **filter-not-403 on `GET /capas`** (doc 18 §5.2, matching records/search/processes) — a no-grant caller now gets `200`+empty (an empty board) instead of the no-access panel; the FE's defensive 403 handling is retained but effectively dead for `/capas`. **⚠ THE structural lesson — the FE-only premise was incomplete: a feature cannot reach its target persona if the board's own LIST read is SYSTEM-gated.** The deferral note + the brief both fixated on the `POST /capas` write (already process-scoped) + the button, and MISSED that `GET /capas` (the board's render gate) was the real chokepoint — Codex P1 caught it; the fix is the same read-filter S-process-scope-2 applied to `/processes`. **⚠ Other traps a future session MUST carry:** (1) **the ruff PostToolUse hook strips just-added imports → body-first** (hit again: `RequestContext`/`authorize`/`gather_grants` were stripped because the body using them came in a later edit). (2) **Mantine's `required` label appends an asterisk to the accessible name** (`getByLabelText("Process")` exact FAILS for a required field → "Process *") — query the required picker by its requireProcess-only PLACEHOLDER ("Pick the owning process"), a genuine discriminator, not the tautological `/^Process/` (which matches both labels) or an exact "(optional)" negative (always null for a required field — the web-test-trap MAJOR was exactly this false-PASS). (3) **the board's "＋ Raise CAPA" open button AND the modal's "Raise CAPA" submit both match `/Raise CAPA/`** while the modal is open → target the modal submit by EXACT `{name:"Raise CAPA"}`; and the board's Severity FILTER (`aria-label="Severity"`) clashes with the modal's Severity while open → scope or avoid. (4) **a backend read-port that flips a list to filter-not-403 must update any PRE-EXISTING test asserting the old 403** (the diff-critic CRITICAL: `test_capa.py::test_capa_read_requires_grant` still asserted `GET /capas`→403; renamed → `test_capa_list_filters_not_403_ncr_still_enforces`, 200+empty while `/ncrs` stays SYSTEM-403). **Named deferrals (not faked):** (i) **the multi-role first-process-probe false-negative** — a caller who is BOTH an auditor (SYSTEM `process.read` → all processes) AND a bound owner of a *non-first* process may have the button hidden (a SAFE false-negative — never a crash/over-grant; server-403 is the boundary); the O(1) probe is the owner-approved trade-off, with a future backend `can_raise` signal the fix if it ever becomes real (Codex re-raised this as a fresh P2, declined-with-rationale). (ii) **NCR raise NOT widened** — `ncr.create` is in the catalog but bound to NO role (SYSTEM-override-only in v1), so no Process-Owner can hold it at any scope → the NCR raise gap is not exercisable by a bound owner (owner-confirmed; the picker would be dead). **Test delta: +5 api integration** (`test_capa_process_scope.py`, CI-only on Windows: list-narrows-to-owned [P1/P2/ad-hoc] · detail+approval-enforce-process-scope [owned 200 / unowned 403] · a SYSTEM `capa.read` holder reads a PROCESS-scoped CAPA [the Top-Mgmt path] · no-grant-list-is-200-empty-not-403 · a bound owner raises ONLY in an owned process [own 201, process-less 403, unowned-P2 403]) **+ the `test_capa.py` 403→200-empty rename/fix; +7 web** (`CapaBoardPage.test.tsx`: button shows for a PROCESS-only `capa.create` holder · hidden for a read-only auditor · the board threads `requireProcess` [placeholder discriminator] · reopen discards the draft; `RaiseCapaModal.test.tsx`: submits the chosen `process_id` · omits the picker when no processes · `requireProcess` gates submit until a pick); **web 1086→1093** (fixtures pinned via `satisfies MePermissions`/`CapaRaiseBody`). ruff + ruff-format + mypy-strict clean (modulo the Windows `O_NOFOLLOW` baseline); redocly clean; CI 11/11 green (all 4 integration shards). **diff-critic CRITICAL** (the stale `GET /capas`→403 assertion) **→ fixed**; **web-test-trap-reviewer MAJOR** (the board required-picker test was a false-PASS — tautological label queries) **→ fixed** (placeholder discriminator + the modal's real submit-gate), plus 2 MINORs (modal-test tautology, persistent-modal reset → conditional mount). **Codex** P1 (board read-filter) + P2 (required picker) FIXED, the fresh multi-role P2 declined-with-rationale; all 3 threads resolved. **Merge gate:** green CI + 0 unresolved threads + reviewers' findings fixed + owner's explicit go. ## v1.x RECORDS PROCESS-SCOPE — Process-Owner record read + authoring + the clause-map grant (the named S-process-scope-1 follow-up; 0057)

> The deferred "records process-scope read" follow-up S-process-scope-1 named after its records read enrichment did NOT converge under Codex and was reverted. Specced first, then shipped in sequenced slices: **spec → R (read) → W (write-enable) → C (clauseMap.read grant)**. The structural insight (from the S-process-scope-1 revert): a READ surface is only safe to scope by process bindings if EVERY write path that CREATES those bindings re-authorizes the target — so the read DECOUPLES from the write (R ships safely with the write gates process-blind), and write-enable (W) is its own sequenced slice with per-target re-auth. The whole records WRITE re-auth is the non-converging surface (Codex took 3–4 rounds each on R + W); **trim-don't-chase** is what converged it.

- **S-records-C** (Process Owner gains `clauseMap.read` @ SYSTEM — the create-in-process wizard's clause step) — **the LAST functional piece of the arc.** A bound Process-Owner (the seeded "Process Owner" role assigned with a PROCESS `bound_scope`, as owner-assignment mints) got **403** on `GET /clauses` (gated `clauseMap.read`, SYSTEM-scoped) → the wizard's clause step was empty. **What shipped (migration `0057`, NO new permission key — `clauseMap.read` already exists [`0004`]; catalog stays 102; R47 = an R38-ADDITIVE role GRANT, not a key):** (1) **migration 0057** grants the Process Owner role a SYSTEM-scoped `clauseMap.read` `role_grant`, inserted for EVERY org's Process Owner role (by role NAME — not the `DEFAULT` org `0004` targets — so it reaches a renamed install like `AHT`; idempotent `on_conflict_do_nothing` on `(org_id,role_id,permission_id)`; data-only → `alembic check` unaffected). (2) **THE coupled resolver fix** in `services/authz/repository._grant_from_role`: the grant alone is INSUFFICIENT — a bound owner's `role_assignment` carries a PROCESS `bound_scope`, and the resolver did `raw = bound_scope or scope_template` (bound_scope REPLACES every grant's scope), so the new SYSTEM `clauseMap.read` got CLAMPED to the bound PROCESS → unsatisfiable against the SYSTEM clause-map resource (`pdp._matches_scope` PROCESS = `bool(scoped & resource.process_ids)`, and a SYSTEM resource has empty `process_ids`). Fix: an **EXPLICIT `level=="SYSTEM"` template is never clamped by a bound_scope** (a SYSTEM-finest grant has no `:assignment_process` placeholder to concretize); every parameterized (PROCESS/FOLDER/…) template still defers to the bound_scope. **⚠ Traps a future session MUST carry:** (1) **`finest_scope` is documentary, but the bound_scope CLAMP is the real blocker** — unlike S-process-scope-2 (where threading `process_ids` was the whole fix), here the SYSTEM grant exists but the bound_scope replace-semantics ate it; the resolver fix is the load-bearing half, not the migration. (2) **blast radius verified = exactly this case** — every pre-existing bound assignment uses `bound_scope={"level":"SYSTEM"}` (a SYSTEM bound + any template = SYSTEM either way → unchanged), and the only PROCESS-bound role today (owner-assignment Process Owner) had NO SYSTEM grant before this slice; no existing SYSTEM grant is widened. (3) **exempt only an EXPLICIT SYSTEM template, not `_scope_from_dict`'s SYSTEM default** — a NULL/level-less template defers to the bound_scope (the conservative, non-widening direction); pre-empts the reviewers' NULL-template note. (4) the ruff hook strips just-added imports (body-first; hit twice here). **Test delta: +1 api unit** (`test_authz_resolver.py`, 5 cases — SYSTEM-not-clamped, PROCESS-still-concretized, SYSTEM-bound-unchanged, no-bound-stays-SYSTEM, level-less-defers; runs LOCALLY) **+1 api integration** (`test_clauses.py::test_bound_process_owner_reads_clauses` — a bound owner reads `/clauses` → 200; discriminates BOTH the migration grant AND the resolver fix) **+ a Process-Owner grant assertion in `test_authz`** (catalog stays 102, the grant is SYSTEM-scoped); **web unchanged.** ruff + format + mypy-strict clean; migration round-trip up↔down↔`alembic check` CLEAN on PG16 (grant verified `Process Owner/clauseMap.read/SYSTEM`, catalog 102). **migration-reviewer + diff-critic both CLEAN** (the NULL-template note pre-empted via the explicit-level exemption); **Codex CLEAN** ("Didn't find any major issues"). **Merge gate:** green CI (11/11) + 0 unresolved threads + reviewers + Codex clean + owner's plan approval (pre-authorized the merge path). PR [#218](https://github.com/CoJoA13/EasySynQ/pull/218), squash `71ecfcf`.

- **S-records-W** (Process-Owner record AUTHORING — write-enable + per-target re-auth) — **enables a bound Process-Owner to AUTHOR records bound to their process, the write half R decoupled from.** **What shipped (NO migration [head stays `0056`], NO new key; contract = gate-note text):** `_record_read_scope` renamed `_record_process_scope`, now resolving BOTH the `_read` AND the per-record `_create_scoped` (write-enable) gates; a new **`_enforce_target_process_record`** (the `documents._enforce_target_process` analogue — re-enforce `record.create` over a scope whose `process_ids` is JUST the target, so a SYSTEM/ARTIFACT/FOLDER holder still passes but a PROCESS holder must own the SPECIFIC target). Re-auth points: **capture** = a per-process loop over the source doc's processes (own ALL; mirrors `documents.create`); **evidence-link add/remove** = re-auth a PROCESS target the caller owns, while EVERY other target type (CLAUSE/DOCUMENT/FINDING/CAPA_STAGE) re-auths over an EMPTY set → broad/SYSTEM holders only (the TRIM — satisfies the spec's R3-2 capa_stage gap by DENY, not by scoping); **correction** = re-auth the UNION of the successor's new-source processes AND the original's FULL effective binding, per-process. `_dispose` stays process-blind. **⚠ THE non-convergence (this surface) — diff-critic CRITICAL + 3 substantive Codex rounds, trim-don't-chase converged it:** the diff-critic caught the **capture untightened** (the base intersection-match passes if ANY source process is owned → a P1-owner could mint a P1+P2 record under a shared doc) → the per-process loop. Codex then surfaced a NEW correction/evidence-link edge each round: **round-4 P1** — the correction re-auth used `source_processes OR effective(original)`, which SHORT-CIRCUITED on an owned source process and skipped an unowned EXISTING binding (a P1-owner could supersede a record co-bound to P2; `capture_correction` does NOT carry the original's EvidenceForLinks → a P1-only successor P2 owners lose) → **replaced the `or` with a UNION** (own every process the original is currently bound to + any new source); **round-5 P2** — a TOCTOU: the correction read the binding BEFORE `capture_correction`'s FOR UPDATE lock, and `link_evidence` inserted without locking the Record → **lock the Record row FOR UPDATE in correction_endpoint (held through the supersede, `populate_existing`), link_evidence, AND unlink_evidence** so all three binding-relevant writers serialize on the one row; **round-6** (2 deeper P2 TOCTOUs — re-auth-under-lock for `link_evidence`, lock the unbounded `correction_of` ancestor chain — + the CAPA-stage residual re-raised) were **TRIMMED as bounded named residuals** (single-org, deep interleavings; the deterministic escalation + same-record TOCTOU are already closed; fixes are unbounded/invasive on a non-converging surface). **⚠ Traps a future session MUST carry:** (1) **a READ surface is only safe to scope by process bindings if EVERY binding-MINTING write re-authorizes the target** — capture (per-process), evidence-link (PROCESS-target), correction (union of the original's full binding); the `_enforce_target_process_record` discipline for EVERY target type. (2) **the records WRITE re-auth does NOT converge — trim, don't chase**: when a surface keeps generating edges round after round, TRIM the over-grant to broad-only/deny (evidence-link non-PROCESS targets) and the FOR UPDATE lock is the STRUCTURAL terminal fix, not another logic patch that invites the next round. (3) the final-state of a correction-vs-link race can't DISTINGUISH the bypass from the legal correction-wins case → prove the lock with a deterministic 2-session held-lock-blocks test, not an `asyncio.gather` final-state assertion. (4) `populate_existing` on the correction's locking load is LOAD-BEARING (the handler reads `original.source_document_id` off the locked object). (5) the ruff hook strips just-added imports (body-first, recurring). **Named residual: `POST /records:init-upload` stays SYSTEM-gated** (process-less byte staging → a Process-Owner authors FORM records + PROCESS links against an already-staged blob, but staging a NEW evidence blob is a bounded follow-up); plus the trimmed Process-Owner CAPA/FINDING/DOCUMENT evidence (broad-only) + the 2 round-6 TOCTOUs. **Test delta: +8 api integration** (`test_records_process_scope.py`: capture-in-owned-process, evidence-link target re-auth add/remove, artifact-holder-not-over-blocked, cannot-introduce-unowned-source, cannot-capture-under-shared-doc, cannot-link-non-process-target, correction-reauths-inherited-binding, correction-cannot-supersede-co-bound [round-4], binding-writes-serialize-on-record-lock [round-5]); **web unchanged.** ruff + format + mypy-strict clean; **diff-critic ×3 (CRITICAL on capture → CLEAN on the union + lock fixes); Codex 3 substantive rounds (4/5/6).** **Merge gate:** green CI (11/11) + 0 unresolved threads (all rounds replied + resolved, round-6 trimmed with rationale) + owner's explicit per-round go. PR [#217](https://github.com/CoJoA13/EasySynQ/pull/217), squash `6dcb976`.

- **S-records-R** (records process-scope READ via a DECOUPLED read-only resolver) — **a bound Process-Owner's PROCESS-scoped `record.read` authorizes records bound to their owned processes, WITHOUT enabling them to mint a binding (the writes stay process-blind; authoring is W).** The decoupling is the spec's central result: a read-only resolver ships safely with NO write re-auth because no NARROW holder can mint a binding (every binding-minting write 403s them at the process-blind base gate). **What shipped (NO migration [head stays `0056`], NO new key — rides `record.read`, `finest_scope` documentary; no contract change):** (1) `services/records/repository.py` = the ONE source of truth — **`record_process_ids`** (leg A `EvidenceForLink(PROCESS)` targets ∪ leg B source-doc `ProcessLink`s), **`record_process_ids_effective`** (+ the R3-1 `correction_of` walk — ITERATIVE, visited-set, no hop cap), and a batched **`record_process_ids_for`** for the list; (2) a new **`_record_read_scope`** resolver (full context + the process binding) for the `_read` gate ONLY — `_create_scoped`/`_dispose` stay on the process-BLIND `_record_scope` (the decoupling); the `GET /records` list row-filter enriched (batched binding + per-row R3-1 fallback); (3) `packs/service.classify_candidates` refactored onto `records_repo.record_process_ids_effective` (the pack classifier + `/records` now agree from one source; the duplicate left `packs/repository`). **3 Codex rounds:** CX-3 hop-cap → **visited set** (cycle-safe, no cap that drops a long legitimate correction chain) + a 2-hop test; the pack-candidate query must ALSO walk corrections (so the pack `record.read` exposure matches the records gate); the candidate "owned" predicate must equal a non-empty own union EXACTLY. **⚠ Traps:** the decoupling (read resolver separate, writes process-blind) is WHY R is safe without W's re-auth — never fold the write gates onto the process-aware resolver without W's `_enforce_target_process_record`. **Test delta: +6 api integration** (`test_records_process_scope.py`: reads-owned/403s-unowned, list-filters, source-less-invisible, R3-1 single + 2-hop correction-chain visibility, + the read/write decoupling invariant — reads 200 but a per-record write 403s); **web unchanged.** ruff + mypy-strict clean; **diff-critic CLEAN (prompted the decoupling-invariant coverage add); Codex 3 rounds.** **Merge gate:** green CI + 0 unresolved threads + Codex clean + owner's go. PR [#216](https://github.com/CoJoA13/EasySynQ/pull/216), squash `1fc8f24`.

- **S-records-spec** (the authz model + sequenced slice plan for "records process-scope read") — **the deferred follow-up, SPECCED + adversarially validated BEFORE code** (the surface that did not converge in S-process-scope-1). `docs/superpowers/specs/2026-06-19-records-process-scope-authz-design.md`: the model + a **4-lens refutation panel** (read-only-safe, 0 holes). **Central result:** enriching a DECOUPLED read-only resolver (read + list only, write gates process-blind) is escalation-free with NO write re-auth — a Process-Owner reads their records but mints nothing (every binding-minting write 403s them at the base gate; capture inherits only the source-doc's already-re-authorized links; the minter enumeration is complete). The write re-auth (the B-work) is needed ONLY to ENABLE Process-Owner authoring, which alone opens the `capa_stage` target class. **Ratified plan: Slice R (read) + Slice W (write-enable, sequenced) + Slice C (`clauseMap.read` → Process-Owner bundle, R38).** Four bounded caveats named as accepted residuals (capture doc-spans-processes visibility, sibling SYSTEM-gated read surfaces, the `correction_of` hop cap, AZ-INV-8 monotonicity). Docs-only. PR [#215](https://github.com/CoJoA13/EasySynQ/pull/215), squash `4e929a9`.

## v1.x OWNER-ASSIGNMENT — PROCESS-scoped RBAC binding: substitutes the long-deferred `:assignment_process` placeholder (0056)

- **S-process-scope-2** (per-process read-filter on `GET /processes` + `/map`) — **"Slice A" of the named S-process-scope-1 "records process-scope read" follow-up: the smallest, lowest-risk, highest-unblock piece, split out from the deeper records work.** A bound Process-Owner's `process.read` is PROCESS-scoped, but the process-landscape reads were gated `require("process.read")` at **default SYSTEM scope** → a bound owner got a hard **403**, so the create-in-process wizard PICKER (shipped #211) was empty for them. **What shipped (BE-only, NO migration [head stays `0056`], NO new permission key [rides `process.read`, catalog stays 102]; contract = description text only — no shape change):** (1) **`GET /processes` + `GET /processes/map`** moved from `Depends(_read)` (SYSTEM enforce) to `Depends(get_current_user)` + a new `_readable_processes()` **row-filter** (`gather_grants("process.read")` once → per-row `authorize` over `ResourceContext(process_ids={str(p.id)})`; the `GET /records` + `/search` precedent). `/map` also **drops any edge whose endpoint is hidden** (no dangling edge to an unreadable process). (2) **`GET /processes/{id}`** moved `_read` → the existing `_read_scoped` (enforce `process.read` at the process's PROCESS scope; still **403-on-deny**, single-resource). (3) the now-unused `_read` (SYSTEM) removed. **THE load-bearing correction (vs the brief, which assumed a migration/finest_scope change):** **no migration and no new key are needed** — the seeded *Process Owner* bundle ALREADY grants `record.read`/`process.read` at PROCESS scope (`0004_seed_authz.py:205,322`), and **`finest_scope` is documentary catalog metadata, NEVER enforced at runtime** (`pdp.py:81-83` matches a PROCESS grant purely on `bool(scoped & resource.process_ids)`); the only blocker was the empty `resource.process_ids` on the read gate. **Decisions/behavior:** a SYSTEM grant matches every row (`_matches_scope` returns True for SYSTEM regardless of `process_ids`) → QMS Owner / Internal Auditor / a `demo` SYSTEM override see the org-wide landscape **byte-identical**; the **one observable change (owner-approved): a no-grant caller on the LIST/MAP now gets `200` + empty instead of `403`** — the documented list-surface **filter-not-403** doctrine (doc 18 §5.2 / doc 15 §9.3), matching records/search (the list/map GETs no longer document a `403`). `GET /clauses` was explicitly **OUT** (a per-process clause filter is ill-defined — clauses are framework-anchored reference data; `clauseMap.read` isn't even in the Process-Owner bundle) → a separate owner decision. **Understand phase** ran a 6-reader → synthesis Workflow that produced the A/B1/B2/B3 split (B1 write-path re-auth BEFORE B2 read scoping is the structural insight from the S-process-scope-1 records revert) and surfaced the no-migration correction. **Codex round 1 — 3 P2, triaged 2-fixed/1-declined (a clean diff-critic passed):** **CX-1** (thread `source_ip`) **FIXED** — `_readable_processes` now threads `request.client.host` so an `ip_allow` grant evaluates exactly as the replaced `require()` enforce did (v1-deferred but kept faithful; the S-leadership-cx1 precedent); **CX-2** (a row-filtered child row leaks its hidden parent's id via `parent_id`) **FIXED** — `_process(p, visible_ids)` nulls `parent_id` on the list/map when the parent isn't visible (the edge-filter rationale; detail/authoring keep it); **CX-3** (honour `include_subprocesses`) **DECLINED** — `include_subprocesses` (docs/07 §5.3, "default true") is documented but **UNIMPLEMENTED anywhere in the v1 PDP** (the PROCESS match is a pure own-id intersection, no resolver walks `parent_id`, owner-assignment mints explicit `process_ids`, `_document_scope`/records/search all use own-id/own-link sets) → a cross-cutting authz-model change that must land consistently across documents/records/processes, named as its own follow-up. **⚠ Traps a future session MUST carry:** (1) **for a process landscape read, `finest_scope` is a red herring — it is documentary, not a runtime gate**; the grant already existed, so the fix was purely threading `process_ids` into the resource context. (2) **a row-filter must sanitize EVERY pointer to a hidden row, not just the rows themselves** — the `/map` edge filter AND the `parent_id` null (CX-2) are the same "no dangling pointer / no hidden-id leak" rule. (3) **the ruff PostToolUse hook strips just-added imports → body-first** (recurring; hit again here). (4) **Slice A converged in ONE Codex round** (the predicted LOW risk) precisely because it's a pure READ with no write-path-minted visibility channel — the opposite of the records read (B2) that didn't converge; the A/B split exists so the safe read ships first. **Deferred (named, not faked) — the rest of "records process-scope read":** **B1** (records evidence-link POST/DELETE + correction RE-AUTHORIZE the target/effective-source process — the `_enforce_target_process` analogue, the safety floor) → **B2** (scope records read by a single shared loader == `packs::record_process_ids`, only after B1) → **B3** (the pre-existing `capa_stage` evidence-link authz gap, orthogonal); plus the `GET /clauses` fix (add `clauseMap.read` SYSTEM to the bundle vs route the wizard's clause step elsewhere — an owner call) and the NEW **subprocess/descendant-inclusion** authz follow-up surfaced by CX-3. **Test delta: +2 api integration** (`test_process_scope.py`: a bound owner of P1-not-P2 narrows on list/map with the P1→P2 edge dropped + a SYSTEM-author full-landscape baseline; a child-owner's `parent_id` nulled while the SYSTEM author sees the real linkage) **+1 assertion + 1 rename in `test_processes.py`** (`test_read_requires_permission` → `test_list_filters_not_403_for_no_grant`, the `200`+empty semantic + detail-still-403; + a SYSTEM-holder `404`-not-`403` detail assertion); **web unchanged** (the FE `useProcesses()` already degrades-on-403 and renders whatever it gets → the picker now populates for a bound owner with no FE change). ruff + ruff-format + mypy-strict clean (modulo the Windows `O_NOFOLLOW` baseline); redocly clean; CI 11/11 green (all 4 integration shards). **diff-critic CLEAN** (SYSTEM-byte-identical, the /map dangling-edge filter, no write-path over-grant channel, the 403-before-404 detail order, the dropped enforce-audit matching records/search, the tests' genuineness all verified — it also prompted the SYSTEM-404 coverage add). **Merge gate:** green CI + 0 unresolved threads (3 Codex P2 — 2 fixed, 1 declined-with-rationale — all replied + resolved) + Codex 👍 re-approve + owner's explicit go.
